Making Up the Missed Sunnah of Fajr: Conditions and Evidence
Ruling on when and how the Sunnah of Fajr is made up

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up the missed Sunnah of Fajr, identify the conditions (time, connection to fard), and explain the hadith evidence and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
The Sunnah of Fajr is made up only before zawal and only if the fard is also missed — an exception to qada being for obligations.

In Hanafi fiqh, making up a missed prayer (qada) is generally reserved for obligatory (fard/wajib) prayers. However, the Sunnah of Fajr holds a special status: it can be made up, but only under strict conditions. This lesson unpacks the ruling found in Nur al-Idah and its commentary, explaining when, how, and for how long the Fajr Sunnah may be performed after its time has passed, along with the prophetic evidence and scholarly differences within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle and the exception
Note the baseline: qada is for obligations. The text then introduces an exception for the Fajr Sunnah, qualifying it with specific conditions.
The exception is based on a specific hadith (khabar), not on qiyas.
2
Determine the time window for qada
The text explicitly states the end time: 'ila al-zawal' (until noon). Confirm that after zawal, no qada is allowed.
Zawal is the moment when the sun passes the meridian, marking the end of the Fajr make-up period.
3
Examine the condition of the fard prayer
The Sunnah is made up only if the fard of Fajr was also missed. It is performed before the fard qada, whether in congregation or alone.
The Sunnah is a 'tabi'' (follower) of the fard; it is not made up independently.
4
Analyze the evidence: hadith of al-Ta'ris
The proof is the Prophet's action on the morning after the night of al-Ta'ris, where he made up both the Sunnah and fard after sunrise. This shows the permissibility but also ties the Sunnah to the fard.
The hadith is a dalil zanni in both thubut and dalalah, but it is sufficient for this ruling.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad holds that the Sunnah can be made up as an independent prayer (maqsuda) before zawal, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf restrict it to being a follower (tab'an). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the latter.
'Ala al-sahih' indicates the preferred view in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم تُقضَ سُنَّةُ الفجر إلا بفَوْتِهَا مع الفرض إلى الزوال، سواء قضى الفرض بجماعة أو منفرداً، فإنه يصلي السنة ثم يقضي الفرض، والقياس أن لا تقضى السنة لاختصاص القضاء بالواجب، لكن ورد الخبر بقضائها قبل الزوال تبعاً للفرض. وما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قَضَاهَا مَعَ الفَرْضِ غَدَاةَ لَيْلَةِ التَعْرِيس بَعْدَ ارْتِفَاعِ الشَّمْس فيبقى ما رواه على الأصل، فلا تقضى وحدها قبل طلوع الشمس ، اتفاقاً، وتقضى بعده قبل الزوال تبعاً اتفاقاً ومقصودة عنــد محمد، ولا تقضى بعد الزوال أصلاً لا مقصودة ولا تبعاً اتفاقاً، على الصحيح.
And the Sunnah of Fajr is not made up except by being missed together with the obligatory prayer until zawal (noon), whether he made up the obligatory prayer in congregation or alone. He prays the Sunnah then makes up the obligatory prayer. Analogy would dictate that the Sunnah is not made up because making up is specific to obligations, but the report has come that it is made up before zawal as a follower of the obligatory prayer. And whatever has been narrated that he, peace be upon him, made it up with the obligatory prayer on the morning of the night of al-Ta'ris after the sun had risen remains according to the original (analogy). So it is not made up alone before sunrise, by agreement, and it is made up after it (sunrise) before zawal as a follower of the obligatory prayer, by agreement, and as an intended (independent) prayer according to Muhammad. And it is not made up after zawal at all, neither as a follower nor as an intended prayer, by agreement, according to the correct view.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding making up the missed Sunnah of Fajr. The general principle is that only obligatory prayers are made up, but the Sunnah of Fajr has an exception: it is made up only if the obligatory Fajr prayer is also missed, and it must be performed before zawal (noon). The text mentions that analogy (qiyas) would suggest no qada for sunnah, but a specific hadith (khabar) allows it as a follower of the fard. The Prophet's practice of making it up after the night of al-Ta'ris is cited. The text clarifies the binding consensus (ittifaq) that it is not made up alone before sunrise, but is made up with the fard before zawal. According to Imam Muhammad, it can be made up as an independent prayer (maqsuda) as well. After zawal, it is not made up at all. This is the sahih position.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed prayer after its prescribed time.
السنّة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): A strongly recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed and rarely left.
الزوال (al-zawal): The time when the sun passes the meridian, i.e., noon; the end of the time for making up Fajr Sunnah in this context.
تبعاً (tab'an): As a follower or dependent on something else; here, the Sunnah is made up subordinately to the fard.
مقصودة (maqsuda): As an intended or independent act; here, making up the Sunnah with its own independent intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, until what time can the missed Sunnah of Fajr be made up?
A) Until sunset.
B) Until the time for Zuhr ends.
C) Until zawal (noon).
D) Until the next Fajr.

Key Takeaway
The missed Sunnah of Fajr is made up only before zawal and only if the fard of Fajr was also missed, as a follower of the fard.

Making Up Missed Rawatib Sunnah Prayers: The Hanafi Position
Ruling with proof on qada of rawatib other than Fajr and the order of making them up

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up missed rawatib sunnah prayers (other than Fajr) and apply the correct order of qada when multiple sunan are missed.

Core Idea
Missed rawatib sunnah prayers are made up only within their fard's time, and the Fajr sunnah takes precedence over the Zuhr sunnah.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies a common confusion: which missed sunan can be made up and in what order? While the Fajr sunnah has a special status, other rawatib (like those before Zuhr) are only made up as followers (tab'an) within the time of their corresponding fard prayer. The text also resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute on the sequence of making up the Fajr and Zuhr sunan when both are missed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule for Qada of Rawatib
Determine the status of making up missed rawatib other than Fajr. The correct view is that they are only made up as followers (tab'an) within the time of the corresponding fard prayer, not independently after the time.
Some shaykhs held they can be made up as followers even outside time, but the correct view restricts it to within time.
2
Recognize the Exception for Fajr Sunnah
Note that the Fajr sunnah (two rak'ahs) is exempted from this rule because of its special emphasis. It can be made up even after its time, as mentioned in the text with reference to earlier discussion.
The Fajr sunnah is the only sunnah that can be made up independently after its time.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Order
When both the Fajr sunnah and the Zuhr sunnah (four rak'ahs before Zuhr) are missed, there is a dispute among the Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the Fajr sunnah is made up first, followed by the Zuhr sunnah. Imam Muhammad holds the opposite order.
The text states that some narrations reverse the positions, but the established view is as above.
4
Note the Mufta Bihi Position and Its Evidence
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the two rak'ahs of Fajr sunnah are performed first, then the four rak'ahs of Zuhr sunnah. This is based on the hadith of Aisha (radiyallahu anha) that the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wasallam) would pray the missed Zuhr sunnah after the Fajr sunnah.
The text cites Sharh al-Kanz and other sources to confirm this as the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما غيرها من السنن فلا تقضى تبعاً إلا في الوقت على الصحيح، وقال بعض المشايخ: إنها تقضى تبعاً؛ لأنه كم من شيء ثبت تبعاً وإن لم يثبت قصداً، كذا في البرهان. وأشار إلى الصحيح بقوله: وقضى السنة التي قبل الظهر في الصحيح عن أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه، وإطلاق القضاء مجازاً كإطلاقه في الحج بعد فساده، إذ ليس له وقت يصير بخروجه قضاء، وفي المعراج: ينوي القضاء عندهما، وعند أبي حنيفة لا ينوي القضاء انتهى. وقيل: لا تقضى لأنه: إنما واظب عليها قبل الظهر في وقته قيد به لأنه لا قضاء بعد خروج الوقت لشيء من السنن إلا سنة الصبح وخصت به لما قدمناه؛ لأن القضاء مختص بالواجبات، فيأتي بالسنة التي قبل الظهر عقبه في وقتِهِ، قبل شفعه على المفتى به، كذا في شرح الكنز للعلامة المقدسي، وقال الكمال: يقضيها عند أبي يوسف بعد الركعتين، وهو قول أبي حنيفة، وعلى قول محمد قبلهما، وقيل: الخلاف بالعكس، انتهى. ونقل الصدر الشهيد: الاختلاف على العكس، وهو الأصح في نقل الخلاف، كما في الدراية، وفي فتاوى العتابي: المختار تقديم الثنتين على الأربع. وفي مبسوط شيخ الإسلام وهو الأصح لحديث عائشة: أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام إذا فاتته الأربع قبل الظهر يصليهن بعد الركعتين وهو قول أبي حنيفة، وكذا في جامع قاضي خان. انتهى. وقال صاحب البحر: وحكم الأربع قبل الجمعة كالتي قبل الظهر، كما لا يخفى. انتهى. فلم يبق إلا التي قبل العشاء، وهي مندوبة فلا مانع من قضائها بعد التي تلي العشاء.
As for other Sunnah prayers, they are not made up as followers except within the time, on the correct view. And some shaykhs said: They are made up as followers because many things are established as followers even if not established independently. So in al-Burhan. And he alluded to the correct view by his statement: 'And he makes up the Sunnah that is before Zuhr, within its time, before its pair, on the correct view from Abu Hanifa and his two companions. And the use of 'qada' here is a metaphor, like its use in Hajj after corruption, since there is no time such that its exit becomes qada. In al-Mi'raj: He intends qada according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), while according to Abu Hanifa he does not intend qada. And it is said: It is not made up because 'he regularly performed it before Zuhr within its time' – this restriction is because there is no qada after the exit of time for any of the Sunnah prayers except the Sunnah of Fajr, and it was singled out due to what we mentioned. Because qada is specific to obligations. So he performs the Sunnah before Zuhr immediately after it (the Fajr Sunnah) within its time, before its pair, upon the fatwa. So in Sharh al-Kanz by al-Allama al-Maqdisi. And al-Kamal said: According to Abu Yusuf, he makes it up after the two rak'ahs, and that is the view of Abu Hanifa; according to Muhammad, before the two rak'ahs; and it is said the difference is reversed. The author of al-Bahr said: The ruling for the four rak'ahs before Jumu'ah is like those before Zuhr. So nothing remains except the (Sunnah) before Isha, which is recommended, so there is no impediment to making it up after the one that follows Isha.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on making up other rawatib (regular Sunnah prayers) that are missed. The correct view is that they are only made up within their prescribed time as followers (tab'an) of the fard, not as independent prayers. However, some shaykhs hold they can be made up as followers even outside time by analogy with other cases. The text then focuses on the Sunnah before Zuhr (the four rak'ahs). According to the correct view, if one misses it, it is made up within the time of Zuhr before the two rak'ahs of Fajr Sunnah (or after? There is a dispute). The text mentions that according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the four rak'ahs are made up after the two rak'ahs of Fajr (i.e., one first makes up the Fajr Sunnah, then the Zuhr Sunnah), while according to Muhammad, it is before. The author prefers the view that the four rak'ahs are prayed after the two. The same applies for the Sunnah before Jumu'ah. The Sunnah before Isha is recommended and can be made up without restriction.

Key Terms
السنن الراتبة (al-sunan al-ratibah): The regular Sunnah prayers associated with the five daily prayers.
الشفع (al-shaf'): In this context, the pair of two rak'ahs, specifically the two rak'ahs of the Fajr Sunnah.
قضاء تبعاً (qada' tab'an): Making up a missed prayer as a follower of another prayer, i.e., not independently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, when making up missed sunan prayers at the time of Zuhr, what is the order?
A) First make up the four rak'ahs of Zuhr sunnah, then the two of Fajr.
B) First make up the two rak'ahs of Fajr sunnah, then the four of Zuhr sunnah.
C) Only make up the Fajr sunnah; the Zuhr sunnah is not made up.
D) They can be made up in any order.

Key Takeaway
Missed rawatib (except Fajr) are made up only within the fard's time as followers, and when both Fajr and Zuhr sunan are missed, the Fajr sunnah takes precedence.

Does Catching Part of a Congregational Prayer Count as Praying in Congregation?
Ruling on latecomer's status in congregation for oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between catching part of a congregational prayer and catching the full prayer to determine whether an oath is broken.

Core Idea
Part of a prayer in congregation is not the whole; for an oath, the entire prayer must be with the Imam.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Nur al-Idah: when a person joins the congregation late and catches only some rak'ahs, does he attain the status of having prayed in congregation? The answer affects not only reward but also the fulfillment of oaths. We will see the settled rule for one or two rak'ahs and then explore a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding three rak'ahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the settled rule
The text agrees that catching one or two rak'ahs of Zuhr does not constitute praying the entire Zuhr in congregation for the purpose of an oath.
This is by consensus (ittifaq) in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the basis
The condition of the oath is praying the full prayer with the Imam; part is not enough. The text states: 'because the condition of his oath is praying Zuhr with the Imam and it did not occur.'
3
Note the agreement on reward
Despite not counting for the oath, the person still attains the virtue (fadl) of congregation by agreement.
Reward is not the same as fulfilling the oath condition.
4
Identify the dispute
The text reports disagreement on whether catching three rak'ahs out of a four-rak'ah prayer (or two out of Maghrib/Witr) counts as full congregation.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school; the text does not name the opposing view.
5
Apply the apparent answer
Based on the apparent answer (zahir al-jawab), the oath is not broken because he prayed only part of it in congregation. The reasoning: 'part of a thing is not the whole.'
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يُصَلِّ الظهر جماعة بإدراك ركعة أو ركعتين اتفاقاً، حتى لو حلف أنه لا يصلي الظهر جماعة أو مع الإمام، ولم يدرك إلا ركعتين أو ركعة لا يحنث؛ لأن شرط حنثه صلاة الظهر مع الإمام ولم تحصل، بل أدرك فضلها أي: فضل الجماعة اتفاقاً، وكذا لو أدرك التشهد يكون مدركاً فضيلتها في قول أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه، وقال الإتقاني: المسبوق يدرك ثواب الجماعة، لكن لا كثواب مدرك أول الصلاة مع الإمام، لفوات التكبيرة الأولى، كذا في شرح المقدسي، واختلف في مدرك الثلاث من الرباعية، وعلى ذلك إدراك ثنتين من المغرب، أو الوتر مع الإمام، فعلى ظاهر الجواب لا يحنث؛ لأنه لم يصلها بل بعضها بجماعة، وبعض الشيء ليس
And he has not prayed Zuhr in congregation by catching one or two rak'ahs, by agreement. So even if he swore that he would not pray Zuhr in congregation or with the Imam, and he caught only two rak'ahs or one rak'ah, he does not break his oath because the condition of his oath is praying Zuhr with the Imam and it did not occur. Rather, he has attained its virtue, i.e., the virtue of congregation, by agreement. And likewise, if he caught the tashahhud, he is considered to have attained its virtue according to Abu Hanifa and his two companions. And al-Itqani said: The person joined later (masbuq) attains the reward of congregation, but not the reward of one who caught the beginning of the prayer with the Imam, due to missing the first takbir. So in Sharh al-Maqdisi. And they differed regarding the one who catches three (rak'ahs) out of a four-rak'ah prayer, and accordingly regarding catching two (rak'ahs) from Maghrib or the witr with the Imam. Based on the apparent answer, he does not break his oath because he did not pray it, but rather part of it in congregation, and part of a thing is not (the whole).
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling of a latecomer (mudrik/masbuq) who joins a congregational prayer after it has started. It states that if a person catches only one or two rak'ahs of the Zuhr prayer in congregation, it is not considered that he prayed the entire Zuhr prayer in congregation. Therefore, if he made an oath not to pray Zuhr in congregation and then he only caught part of it, his oath is not broken because the condition of the oath is not fulfilled. However, he still attains the virtue of congregation. There is an agreement (ittifaq) on this. If he catches only the tashahhud, the same applies. Al-Itqani notes that the masbuq gets reward but not as much as the one who started from the beginning because of missing the first takbir. Then the text mentions a dispute regarding a person who catches three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer (i.e., only one rak'ah missed) – is he considered to have prayed in congregation? The text does not give a definitive resolution here, but indicates that according to the apparent answer, the oath is not broken because he did not pray the entire prayer in congregation.

Key Terms
مدرك (mudrik): A person who joins the congregation after the Imam has started but catches at least one rak'ah.
فضل الجماعة (fadl al-jama'ah): The virtue or reward of praying in congregation.
الحنث (al-hinth): The breaking of an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person swore he would not pray Zuhr in congregation, and then he joined the congregation but only caught two rak'ahs, what is the ruling?
A) He has broken his oath because he prayed part of Zuhr in congregation.
B) He has not broken his oath because he did not pray the entire Zuhr prayer in congregation.
C) He has not broken his oath only if he caught at least three rak'ahs.
D) His oath is void because he intended the full prayer.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, catching part of a congregational prayer does not count as having prayed the entire prayer in congregation for the fulfillment of oaths; only catching all rak'ahs does.

Making Up the Sunnah Before Zuhr: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on making up missed sunnah before zuhr after catching congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding making up the missed sunnah before zuhr when joining late, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Hanafis allow making up the sunnah before zuhr within its time, but disagree on intention and order.

When a person joins the zuhr congregation late and misses the sunnah before zuhr, may he make it up? While the general Hanafi rule is that no sunnah is made up after its time except Fajr, this case is an exception. In this lesson, we examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on how and when to perform this make-up, and which ruling is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the issue
The person catches part of the congregation and misses the four rak'ahs before zuhr. The issue: can he make them up, and if so, how?
The sunnah before zuhr is a mu'akkadah sunnah.
2
Understand the general principle
Sunnah prayers are not made up after their time except Fajr. This is the default rule.
3
Examine the exception for sunnah before zuhr
Some scholars allow making it up within its time, using the term qada' metaphorically. Note the dispute on intention: Abu Hanifa says do not intend qada', Sahibayn say intend qada'.
The term qada' is metaphorical here because it is performed within the same time.
4
Analyze the dispute on order
After the two obligatory rak'ahs or before? Three views: Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf say after the two, Muhammad says before, and some report the opposite.
The hadith of Aisha is cited as evidence for the order.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is to perform it before the shaf' (the two sunnah after zuhr), with intention of qada' according to Sahibayn.
This is based on the preferred view of later scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقضى السنَّةَ الَّتي قبل الظهر، في وقته، قبلَ شَفْعِهِ. ولم يُصَلِّ الظهر جماعة بإدراك ركعة، بل أدرك فضلها واخْتُلِفَ فِي مُدْرِكِ الثّلاثِ.. السنن فلا تقضى تبعاً إلا في الوقت على الصحيح، وقال بعض المشايخ: إنها تقضى تبعاً؛ لأنه كم من شيء ثبت تبعاً وإن لم يثبت قصداً، كذا في البرهان. وأشار إلى الصحيح بقوله: وقضى السُنَّةَ التي قبل الظهر في الصحيح عن أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه، وإطلاق القضاء مجازاً كإطلاقه في الحج بعد فساده، إذ ليس له وقت يصير بخروجه قضاء، وفي المعراج: ينوي القضاء عندهما، وعند أبي حنيفة لا ينوي القضاء انتهى. وقيل: لا تقضى لأنه: إنما واظب عليها قبل الظهر في وقته. قيد به لأنه لا قضاء بعد خروج الوقت لشيء من السنن إلا سنة الصبح وخصصت به لما قدمناه؛ لأن القضاء مختص بالواجبات، فيأتي بالسنة التي قبل الظهر عقبه في وقتِهِ، قبل شَفْعِهِ على المفتى به، كذا في شرح الكنز للعلامة المقدسي، وقال الكمال: يقضيها عند أبي يوسف بعد الركعتين، وهو قول أبي حنيفة، وعلى قول محمد قبلهما، وقيل: الخلاف بالعكس، انتهى. ونقل الصدر الشهيد: الاختلاف على العكس، وهو الأصح في نقل الخلاف، كما في الدراية، وفي فتاوى العتابي: المختار تقديم الثنتين على الأربع. وفي مبسوط شيخ الإسلام وهو الأصح لحديث عائشة: أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام إذا فاتته الأربع قبل الظهر يصليهن بعد الركعتين، وهو قول أبي حنيفة، وكذا في جامع قاضي خان. انتهى. وقال صاحب البحر: وحكم الأربع قبل الجمعة كالتي قبل الظهر، كما لا يخفى. انتهى. فلم يبق إلا التي قبل العشاء، وهي مندوبة فلا مانع من قضائها بعد التي تلي العشاء.
And he makes up the sunnah before zuhr, in its time, before its doubling. And he did not pray zuhr in congregation by catching a rak'ah, but rather caught its virtue, and there is disagreement regarding the one who catches three. The sunan are not made up as a consequence except in the time, according to the correct view. And some scholars said: they are made up as a consequence because there are many things that are established as a consequence even if not established intentionally, as in al-Burhan. And he alluded to the correct view by saying: he makes up the sunnah before zuhr according to the correct view from Abu Hanifa and his two companions, and the use of 'making up' is metaphorical, like its use in Hajj after it becomes invalid, because it has no time that by its exit becomes a make-up. And in al-Mi'raj: he intends make-up according to them, and according to Abu Hanifa he does not intend make-up, end. And it was said: it is not made up because 'he only regularly performed it before zuhr in its time.' He restricted it because there is no make-up after the exit of the time for any of the sunan except the sunnah of Fajr, and it was specified for it due to what we presented, because make-up is specific to obligatory acts. So he performs the sunnah before zuhr after it, in its time, before its doubling, according to the mufta bihi, as in Sharh al-Kanz by al-Maqdisi. And al-Kamal said: he makes it up according to Abu Yusuf after the two rak'ahs, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa, and according to Muhammad before them, and it was said the disagreement is the opposite, end. And al-Sadr al-Shahid transmitted the disagreement is the opposite, and it is the most correct in transmitting the disagreement, as in al-Diraya. And in Fatawa al-Atabi: the chosen is to put the two before the four. And in Mabsoot of Shaykh al-Islam, it is the most correct according to the hadith of Aisha that when the four before zuhr were missed, he would pray them after the two rak'ahs, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifa, and likewise in Jami' Qadi Khan. End. And the author of al-Bahr said: the rule of the four before Jumu'ah is like those before zuhr, as is not hidden. End. So nothing remains except the one before Isha, and it is recommended, so there is no impediment to making it up after that which follows Isha.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether and how to make up the sunnah prayer before zuhr when one joins the congregation late and misses it. The author begins by stating the ruling from the matn: the person who catches only part of the congregation makes up the sunnah before zuhr in its time before the shaf' (the two rak'ahs that are the sunnah after zuhr?). The correct view is that sunnah prayers are not made up after their time, except for the sunnah of Fajr. However, some scholars allow making them up as a consequence (taba'an). The author clarifies that the term 'make up' (qada') is used metaphorically here because there is no specific time for qada' of sunnah. There is also disagreement about the intention: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, one should intend qada', while Abu Hanifa says not to. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is to perform the missed sunnah before the shaf' (the two rak'ahs after zuhr?) according to the majority. A further dispute arises on the order: after the two rak'ahs (sunna mu'akkada?) or before? The preferred view is to pray the two before the four, based on the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet would make up the four before zuhr after the two rak'ahs. The author concludes that the same rule applies to the four before Jumu'ah, and the only remaining issue is the sunnah before Isha, which is recommended and can be made up at any time.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Compensation for a missed act of worship by performing it after its prescribed time. Here used metaphorically because the sunnah is performed within the same time.
شافع (shaf'): The two rak'ahs that are the sunnah after the obligatory prayer of zuhr, also called the shaf'.
المفتى به (al-mufta bihi): The relied-upon position for issuing fatwa, which is the view preferred by later scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on making up the sunnah prayer before zuhr for someone who joined the congregation late?
A) It must be made up later in the day.
B) It is not made up at all.
C) It is made up in its time, before the shaf' prayer.
D) It is only made up if missed unintentionally.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah before zuhr can be made up within its time before the shaf' with intention of qada', according to the mufta bihi.

Catching Three Rak'ahs and Its Effect on Oaths
Intra-Hanafi dispute on congregation for oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on whether catching three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah congregation breaks an oath to avoid congregation, and explain the evidentiary basis of each.

Core Idea
Catching most of a congregation does not break an oath to avoid it—part of a thing is not the thing.

This passage reveals an internal Hanafi debate: if a person swears not to pray zuhr in congregation, then catches three of its four rak'ahs with the imam, does his oath break? The majority says no; Shams al-A'imma says yes. Their disagreement turns on whether the 'majority has the ruling of the whole' in the context of oaths. By analyzing the evidence, you will learn how Hanafi jurists weigh principles and analogies.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and its context
The issue: a person swears not to pray zuhr in congregation, then catches three of four rak'ahs with the imam. Does he break his oath?
The same question applies to catching two of three rak'ahs in Maghrib or Witr.
2
Identify the majority Hanafi position and its evidence
Majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad): he does not break his oath because 'part of a thing is not the thing'.
They analogize to an oath not to eat a loaf: eating most does not fulfill it.
3
Identify the position of Shams al-A'imma and his evidence
Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi: he breaks his oath because 'the majority has the ruling of the whole'.
He supports this with the case of swearing not to read a surah: reading all but one letter still breaks the oath.
4
Analyze the supporting evidence from oaths
The passage also cites the loaf analogy (agreed upon) and the surah case (with exceptions). These show that the 'majority' principle is not absolute in oaths.
The surah case has an exception: missing a long verse does not break the oath.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: if a person catches three rak'ahs, the majority says oath is intact, Shams al-A'imma says it is broken. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
Al-Fath and the author prefer the first view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يُصَلِّ الظهر جماعة بإدراك (ركعة) أو ركعتين اتفاقاً، حتى لو حلف أنه لا يصلي الظهر جماعة أو مع الإمام، ولم يدرك إلا ركعتين أو ركعة لا يحنث؛ لأن شرط حنثه صلاة الظهر مع الإمام ولم تحصل، بل أدرك فضلها أي فضل الجماعة اتفاقاً، وكذا لو أدرك التشهد يكون مدركاً فضيلتها في قول أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه، وقال الإتقاني: المسبوق يدرك ثواب الجماعة، لكن لا كثواب مدرك أول الصلاة مع الإمام، لفوات التكبيرة الأولى، كذا في شرح المقدسي، واختُلِفَ في مُدْرِكِ الثَّلاثِ من الرباعية، وعلى ذلك إدراك ثنتين من المغرب، أو الوتر مع الإمام، فعلى ظاهر الجواب لا يحنث؛ لأنه لم يصلها بل بعضها بجماعة، وبعض الشيء ليس بالشيء. واختار شمس الأئمة: أنه يحنث لأن للأكثر حكم الكل، والظاهر الأول، كما في الفتح. ومما يضعف قول شمس الأئمة السرخسي ما اتفقوا عليه في باب الأيمان: أنه لو حلف لا يأكل هذا الرغيف لا يحنث إلا بأكل كله فإن الأكثر لا يقوم مقام الكل، لكن في الخلاصة: لو حلف لا يقرأ سورة فقرأها إلا حرفاً حنث ولو قرأها إلا آية طويلة لا يحنث، كذا في البحر، وفي الكافي: لو قال: عبده حر إن أدرك الظهر، فإنه يحنث بإدراك ركعة؛ لأن إدراك الشيء بإدراك آخره يقال: أدرك أيامه أي آخرها، وفي الخلاصة: لو قال: عبده حر إن أدرك الظهر مع الإمام، فأدرك الإمام في التشهد ودخل معه في صلاته حنث، كذا في شرح المقدسي.
And he did not pray zuhr in congregation by catching (one) rak'ah or two rak'ahs, by agreement. So if he swore that he would not pray zuhr in congregation or with the imam, and he only caught two rak'ahs or one rak'ah, he does not break his oath, because the condition of his oath is praying zuhr with the imam, and it did not happen. Rather, he caught its virtue, i.e., the virtue of the congregation, by agreement. Likewise, if he caught the tashahhud, he catches its virtue according to Abu Hanifa and his two companions. And al-Itqani said: the follower who is preceded catches the reward of the congregation, but not like the reward of the one who catches the beginning of the prayer with the imam, due to missing the first takbir, as in Sharh al-Maqdisi. And there is disagreement regarding the one who catches three of a four-rak'ah prayer, and likewise catching two of Maghrib or Witr with the imam. According to the apparent answer, he does not break his oath, because he did not pray it but rather some of it in congregation, and part of a thing is not the thing. And Shams al-A'imma chose that he breaks his oath because the majority has the ruling of the whole. And the apparent is the first, as in al-Fath. And what weakens the saying of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi is what they agreed upon in the chapter of oaths: that if he swore not to eat this loaf, he does not break his oath unless he eats all of it, because the majority does not stand in the place of the whole. But in al-Khulasa: if he swore not to read a surah, and he read it except one letter, he breaks his oath; but if he read it except a long verse, he does not break his oath, as in al-Bahr. And in al-Kafi: if he said, 'his slave is free if he catches the zuhr prayer,' then he breaks his oath by catching one rak'ah, because catching a thing is by catching its end; it is said, 'he caught his days,' meaning its end. And in al-Khulasa: if he said, 'his slave is free if he catches the zuhr prayer with the imam,' and he caught the imam in tashahhud and entered with him in his prayer, he breaks his oath, as in Sharh al-Maqdisi.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal implications of catching only part of the congregational prayer, specifically in the context of oaths. The author begins by stating the agreed-upon ruling: if someone prays zuhr but catches only one or two rak'ahs with the congregation, he is not considered to have prayed in congregation for the purpose of an oath. He merely caught the virtue of congregation. However, there is disagreement about catching three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer, or two rak'ahs of Maghrib or Witr. The apparent answer is that this does not break the oath, because part of a thing is not the thing itself. Shams al-A'imma (al-Sarakhsi) held the opposite view, applying the principle that the majority has the ruling of the whole. The author then discusses supporting evidence from oaths about eating a loaf or reading a surah, showing that the matter is nuanced. The practical outcome differs based on the wording of the oath.

Key Terms
مدرك الثلاث (mudrik al-thalath): One who catches three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer with the imam, missing only the first rak'ah.
فضل الجماعة (fadl al-jama'ah): The virtue or reward of praying in congregation, which is attained even if one joins late.
حنث (hanith): The breaking of an oath; the legal consequence of failing to fulfill one's vow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent answer in the passage, if someone swears not to pray zuhr in congregation and he catches three rak'ahs, does he break his oath?
A) Yes, because the majority has the ruling of the whole.
B) No, because part of a thing is not the thing.
C) Yes, because catching three rak'ahs is like catching all.
D) No, because he did not pray with the imam at all.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, for oaths, the majority does not stand for the whole; thus, catching most of a congregation does not break an oath to avoid it.

When Voluntary Prayer Before the Obligatory is Permissible
Ruling on permissibility of voluntary prayer before obligatory prayer when time is limited

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing voluntary (nafl) prayer before the fard prayer and apply it to scenarios involving limited time and impurity on the garment.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer before fard is allowed only if you are certain not to miss the fard time.

You might think you can always pray extra nafl before the fard prayer, but the Shariah imposes a crucial condition: you must be confident that the obligatory prayer time will not expire. This lesson explains when nafl before fard is permitted, the evidence from the Sunnah, and a practical scenario involving minor impurity on the garment. Understanding this principle helps you prioritize the obligatory over the voluntary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing a voluntary (nafl) prayer before the obligatory (fard) prayer. The ruling is that it is permitted (sunnah ghayr muakkadah) only if one is safe from missing the fard time; otherwise it is prohibited.
The condition is 'amn min fawt al-waqt' – security from loss of time.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'When the prayer is established, no prayer except the obligatory.' This is a proof that once the iqamah is called, all voluntary prayers must stop, indicating the priority of the fard.
The hadith is narrated by Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لا صلاة إلا المكتوبة' (no prayer except the obligatory) is a general prohibition of any non-obligatory prayer at the time of iqamah. By extension, if the time is so short that the fard may be missed, the same prohibition applies to starting a nafl before the fard.
The Hanafi usul principle: a general command (nahy) indicates prohibition.
4
Apply the expansion scenario
The passage expands to a situation where a person has a minor impurity (less than a dirham) on his garment and fears missing the congregation or the time. The ruling: it is recommended (mustahab) to pray with the congregation despite the impurity, rather than washing and missing it. If there is no fear, it is better to wash and restart the prayer.
This shows that preserving the congregation and time takes precedence over removing a minor impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتطوّع قبل الفرضِ إِنْ أَمِنَ فَوْتَ الوقتِ، وإلا فلا. وإذا أقيمت الصلاة فلا صلاة إلا المكتوبة. وإذا خشي فوت الجماعة أو الوقت، وعلى ثوبه نجاسة أقل من الدرهم، استحب له الصلاة مع الجماعة وأداء الفرض في وقته، وإن لم يخش ولو بإدراك الجماعة في موضع آخر، فالأفضل أن يغسل ثوبه ويستقبل الصلاة بعد شروعه فيها؛ ليكون مؤدياً للجائز بيقين، كذا في التجنيس والمزيد.
And he performs voluntary prayer before the obligatory if he is safe from the loss of the time, and if not, then he does not. And when the prayer is established, there is no prayer except the obligatory. And if he fears loss of congregation or time, and on his garment there is impurity less than a dirham, it is recommended for him to pray with the congregation and perform the obligatory in its time. And if he does not fear, even if he can catch the congregation in another place, then it is better that he wash his garment and restart the prayer after beginning it, so that he may perform the permissible with certainty, as in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on performing voluntary (nafl) prayers before the obligatory prayer. The general principle is that one may pray nafl before fard only if he is sure that he will not miss the fard time. If the time is narrow, he should not pray nafl. The hadith 'When the prayer is established, no prayer except the obligatory' is cited as evidence. The author then discusses a scenario where a person fears missing the congregation or the time, and there is a minor impurity (less than a dirham) on his garment. In such a case, it is recommended to pray with the congregation and perform the fard in its time, rather than washing the garment and missing the congregation. If there is no such fear, it is better to wash the garment and repeat the prayer after beginning it, so as to perform it with certainty of ritual purity.

Key Terms
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary, non-obligatory prayer performed as an act of devotion.
فوت الوقت (fawt al-waqt): The departure of the prescribed time for a prayer, after which it must be made up.
نجاسة (najasah): Impurity, such as blood or urine, that affects ritual purity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One must be sure that the obligatory prayer time will not be lost.
C) One must be in a state of wudu.
D) The mosque must be nearby.

Key Takeaway
Before performing any voluntary nafl prayer before the fard, ensure you have enough time to complete the fard before its time expires.

Catching the Rak'ah: Joining the Imam in Ruku'
Ruling on catching the rak'ah by joining imam in ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for catching a rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku' and identify the evidence from the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
You catch the rak'ah only by performing ruku' with the imam before he raises his head.

A latecomer to congregational prayer often arrives when the imam is already bowing. Many assume that simply uttering the takbir suffices, but the Hanafi school emphasizes the physical act of bowing in time. This lesson unpacks the precise ruling and the proof from the Companion Ibn Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is joining the congregation when the imam is in ruku'. The ruling is that the rak'ah is caught only if a specific condition is met.
The condition is the key.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the statement of Abdullah ibn Umar, which is either a marfu' hadith or a companion saying. It is cited in the passage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The conditional phrasing 'if you perform ruku' before he raises his head, then you have caught the rak'ah' directly indicates that catching is contingent on bowing before the imam rises.
This is a clear linguistic indicator.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school or among the four schools on this point; it is mutually agreed upon.
Mutaffaq alayh.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling is that the follower must perform ruku' while the imam is still in ruku', before the imam raises his head.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أدرك إمامه راكعاً فكبر، ووقف حتى رفع الإمام رأسه من الركوع، أو لم يقف بل انحط بمجرد إحرامه فرفع الإمام رأسه قبل ركوع المؤتم لم يدرك الركعة؛ لقول ابن عمر: إذا أدركت الإمام راكعاً فركعت قبل أن يرفع رأسه فقد أدركت الركعة، فإن رفع قبل أن تركع فقد فاتتك تلك الركعة. انتهى.
And whoever catches his imam in ruku', and he says the takbir and stands (waiting) until the imam raises his head from ruku', or he does not stand but lowers himself immediately upon his ihram, and then the imam raises his head before the follower's ruku', he does not catch the rak'ah, according to the statement of Ibn Umar: 'When you catch the imam in ruku' and you perform ruku' before he raises his head, then you have caught the rak'ah. If he raises before you perform ruku', then that rak'ah has been missed for you.' End.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage provides a clear ruling on a common scenario: a latecomer joins the congregation when the imam is in the ruku' position. The key condition for catching the rak'ah is that the follower must perform the ruku' (bowing) with the imam before the imam raises his head. If the follower merely says the takbir and waits, or even descends to ruku' after the imam has already lifted, he does not catch that rak'ah. The evidence is the statement of Abdullah ibn Umar, which is a marfu' hadith (attributed to the Prophet) or a companion statement. The ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position that the part of prayer that defines the rak'ah is the ruku'.

Key Terms
أدرك الركعة (adraka al-rak'ah): To catch a unit of prayer by joining the imam before or during the ruku'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Perform ruku' before the imam raises his head.
C) Wait for the imam to finish ruku' and then join.
D) Recite a brief surah before the ruku'.

Key Takeaway
The rak'ah is caught by performing ruku' with the imam before he raises his head.

Voluntary Prayer Before Obligatory Prayer: Conditions and Exceptions
Ruling with proof on voluntary prayer before fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for performing voluntary prayer before the obligatory prayer and identify when it becomes prohibited.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer before fard is only allowed when you are certain you will not miss the fard or its congregation.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on performing supererogatory (nafl) prayers before the obligatory prayer. While such prayers are generally recommended, they become prohibited if they risk missing the fard prayer or a rak'ah of the congregation. We will explore the evidence, the rationale behind the condition, and a practical exception regarding impurity on the garment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing voluntary prayer (tatawwu') before the obligatory prayer. The basic ruling is that it is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized) when the condition of safety from missing the fard is met.
Voluntary includes both rawatib and nafl.
2
State the condition
The condition is 'amn al-fawt' – being secure from missing the time of the fard or missing a rak'ah of the congregational prayer (for prayers other than Fajr). If this condition is absent, the voluntary becomes prohibited.
The prohibition is based on the hadith: 'When the iqamah is called, there is no prayer except the obligatory one.'
3
Recognize the exception for Fajr
For Fajr, the sunnah before the fard is performed even after the iqamah, as previously established in the text. This exception is due to its specific virtue.
This is an exception to the general rule.
4
Understand the rationale
The text gives two reasons: (1) the solitary worshipper's prayer is deficient and voluntary prayers compensate; (2) voluntary prayers before fard cut off the hope of Satan, who tempts one to neglect obligations.
This rationale emphasizes prioritizing obligations.
5
Apply to the impurity exception
If one fears missing the congregation and has impurity less than a dirham on his garment, it is recommended to join the congregation and pray on time rather than washing and missing it. If there is no risk, washing and restarting is better.
This shows the principle of preserving the obligatory act.

ويتطوّع قبل الفرضِ إِنْ أَمِنَ فَوْتَ الوقتِ) وأمن فوت ركعة مع الجماعة، في غير الصبح كما تقدم، وسواء تطوع بمؤكدة أو غيرها، مقيماً كان أو مسافراً، منفرداً أو بجماعة، سائراً أو نازلاً، لأن المنفرد أحوج إلى المكمل لنقصان صلاته من وجه والسنة شرعت قبل المكتوبة لقطع طمع الشيطان، فإنه يقول: من لم يطعني في ترك ما لم يكتب عليه، فكيف يطيعني في ترك ما كتب عليه؟! والمنفرد في ذلك أحوج وهو أصح، والأخذ به أحوط، وهذا في حقنا، أما في حقه فزيادة الدرجات، إذ لا خلل في صلاته ولا طمع للشيطان فيها، كما في « الدراية»، و «الفتح»، و « العناية»، (وإلأ ) أي : إن لم يأمن الـفـوت بـأن ضاق الوقت، أو لم يضق ولكن تفوته الجماعة بركعة في غير الفجر، (فلا) يتطوع؛ لأن الاشتغال بما يفوت به الأداء لا يجوز، « وإذا أقيمت الصلاة فلا صلاة إلا المكتوبة ) (۳)، وإذا خشي فـوت الجماعة أو الوقت، وعلى ثوبه نجاسة أقل من الدرهم، استحب له الصلاة مع الجماعة وأداء الفرض في وقته، وإن لم يخش ولو بإدراك الجماعة في موضع آخر، فالأفضل أن يغسل ثوبه ويستقبل الصلاة بـعـد شــروعـه فيها؛ ليكون مؤدياً للجائز بيقين، كذا في ( التجنيس والمزيد » .
And he may perform voluntary prayer before the obligatory prayer if he is safe from missing the time, and safe from missing a rak'ah with the congregation, other than for Fajr as previously stated. It is the same whether he performs an emphasized or non-emphasized voluntary prayer, whether he is a resident or a traveler, alone or with a congregation, traveling or stationary, because the one who prays alone is more in need of completion for the deficiency in his prayer in one respect, and the Sunnah was prescribed before the obligatory prayer to cut off the hope of Satan. For he (Satan) says: 'He who does not obey me in neglecting what was not prescribed for him, how will he obey me in neglecting what was prescribed for him?' And the one who prays alone is more in need of that, and it is more correct, and acting upon it is more precautionary. This is for us (ordinary people). As for him (the perfect believer), it is a means of increasing stations, for there is no deficiency in his prayer and no hope for Satan in it. As in al-Diraya, al-Fath, and al-Inaya. (And if not), i.e., if he is not safe from missing the time in that the time is narrow, or it is not narrow but he misses a rak'ah of the congregation in prayers other than Fajr, then he should not perform voluntary prayer, because occupying oneself with what causes missing the performance is not permissible. And the hadith: 'When the prayer is established, there is no prayer except the obligatory prayer.' And if he fears missing the congregation or the time, and on his garment there is impurity less than a dirham, it is recommended for him to pray with the congregation and perform the obligatory prayer in its time. And if he does not fear, even if he can catch the congregation elsewhere, the better is that he wash his garment and restart the prayer after having started it, to be performing the permissible with certainty. As in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid.

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on performing voluntary (nafl) prayer before the obligatory (fard) prayer. The key condition is that one must be confident that he will not miss the time of the fard nor miss a rak'ah of the congregational prayer (for non-Fajr prayers). The ruling applies generally: whether the voluntary is an emphasized sunnah (like the rawatib) or a non-emphasized nafl, whether one is resident or traveling, praying alone or in congregation. The rationale given is that the solitary worshipper's prayer is deficient in terms of reward, and voluntary prayers compensate for that. Furthermore, voluntary prayers before fard cut off the hope of Satan, who tempts one to neglect both. The text also clarifies that if there is a risk of missing the fard time or congregation, voluntary prayer is forbidden (indicated by 'la yatawwa''). This is supported by the hadith: 'When the iqamah is called, there is no prayer except the obligatory one.' An exception is discussed regarding impurity on the garment: if one fears missing the congregation while having impurity smaller than a dirham, it is recommended to join the congregation and pray on time, rather than washing and missing the congregation. If there is no risk, the better is to wash and restart the prayer. This reflects the Hanafi principle of prioritising the obligatory over the voluntary.

Key Terms
التطوع (al-tatawwu'): Voluntary act of worship, here specifically referring to supererogatory prayer before the obligatory prayer.
أمن الفوت (amina al-fawt): Being secure from missing the obligatory prayer (its time or congregation).

Catching a Rak'ah with the Imam: Conditions and Rulings
Details the ruling on catching a rak'ah, including conditions and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for catching a rak'ah in congregational prayer and apply it to scenarios where the follower joins late, identifying when the rak'ah is caught or missed.

Core Idea
A rak'ah is caught by sharing ruku' or part of qiyam with the imam; missing ruku' before the imam rises means the rak'ah is lost.

Joining the congregation late raises a critical question: when have you actually caught a full unit (rak'ah) with the imam? This passage, based on a statement of Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), clarifies the precise condition. It also addresses related scenarios such as the follower who misses ruku', the number of takbirs required, and what happens if one catches the imam in the final sitting. Understanding this ruling is essential for every muqtadi to ensure the validity of his prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is the follower (muqtadi) catching a rak'ah with the imam. The ruling is that if the condition is met, he has caught the rak'ah and does not need to make it up; otherwise, he must compensate.
The overall prayer remains valid as long as the conditions for catching are met.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the statement of Ibn 'Umar (radiyallahu anhu) which is a marfoo' hadith (attributed to the Prophet ﷺ). The passage quotes it: 'If you catch the imam in ruku' and bow before he raises his head, you have caught the rak'ah; if he raises his head before you bow, that rak'ah has escaped you.'
This hadith is ahad (single narrator), so its thubut is zanni, but its dalalah (meaning) is clear (qati').
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit conditional phrase 'if you bow before he raises his head' indicates that the catch depends solely on bowing (ruku') before the imam's head rise. The commentary then expands: sharing any part of the standing (qiyam) or ruku' (which has the ruling of standing) achieves the catch.
Thus, two alternative conditions are established: share qiyam OR share ruku' in time.
4
Analyze the exceptions and distinctions
The passage then details: (a) if the follower misses ruku', he must still follow the imam in sujud; (b) if he bows alone then joins in sujud, it's valid because only an extra ruku' was added; (c) if he enters after imam's first sujud and performs a full rak'ah alone, it invalidates the prayer; (d) if he catches the imam in the final sitting and stands to recite, his recitation is not counted.
These distinctions hinge on whether an extra ruku' or an extra full rak'ah is introduced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أدرك إمامه راكعاً فكبر ووقف حتى رفع الإمام رأسَهُ من الركوع أو لم يقف بل انحط بمجرد إحرامه فرفع الإمام رأسه قبل ركوع المؤتم لم يُدْرِكِ الركعة؛ لقول ابن عمر : ( إذا أدركت الإمام راكعاً فركعت قبل أن يرفع رأسه فقد أدركت الركعة، فإن رفع قبل أنْ تَركَعَ فقد فاتتك تلك الركْعَةَ ) انتهى. فكان الشرط لإدراك الركعة إما مشاركة الإمام في جزء من القيام وإن لم يشاركه في الركوع أو في جزء مما له حكم القيام وهو الركوع وإن لم يشاركه في القيام ولا يشترط الإتيان بتكبيرتين للإحرام والركوع خلافاً لبعضهم ولو كبر قائماً ينوي بتلك التكبيرة الركوع والافتتاح جاز ولغت نيته كما في «الفتح». تنبيه: يجب على المقتدي إذا فاته الركوع متابعة الإمام في السجود وإن لم يحسب له من الصلاة وإن لم يتابعه ووقف حتى قام ثم تابعه في بقية الصلاة وقضى ما فاته من الركعات بعد فراغ الإمام تجوز صلاته؛ لأنه يصلي تلك الركعة الفائتة بسجدتيها ولو ركع وحده ثم شارك الإمام في السجدتين لا تفسد صلاته فرق بين هذا وبين ما إذا ركع الإمام وسجد سجدة ورفع رأسه عنها فجاء رجل ودخل معه وركع وسجد سجدتين فسدت صلاته والفرق أنَّ في المسألة الأولى لم يدخل فيها إلا زيادة ركوع لأنه قد وجب عليه متابعة الإمام في السجدتين وذا لا يفسد الصلاة أما هاهنا وجه إدخال زيادة ركعة وهو الركوع والسجود، وإن أدرك الإمام في القعدة الأخيرة ولم يقعد معه ولكن قام وقرأ فما وجد من القيام والقراءة قبل فراغ الإمام من التشهد لا يكون معتبراً كذا في التجنيس والمزيد
And whoever catches his imam in ruku', so he says takbir and stands until the imam raises his head from ruku', or he does not stand but bends down immediately upon his ihram, and the imam raises his head before the follower's ruku', he has not caught the rak'ah; due to the statement of Ibn 'Umar: 'If you catch the imam in ruku' and you bow before he raises his head, you have caught the rak'ah; if he raises his head before you bow, that rak'ah has escaped you.' End. So the condition for catching the rak'ah is either sharing with the imam in part of the standing, even if he does not share in the ruku', or in a part that has the ruling of standing, which is ruku', even if he does not share in the standing. And it is not required to perform two takbirs for ihram and ruku', contrary to some. And if he says takbir while standing, intending by that takbir both ruku' and opening, it is permissible and his intention is void, as in al-Fath. Note: It is obligatory for the follower who misses the ruku' to follow the imam in the prostration, even if it is not counted for him from the prayer. And if he does not follow him and stands until he rises, then follows him in the rest of the prayer and makes up the missed rak'ahs after the imam finishes, his prayer is valid, because he performs that missed rak'ah with its two prostrations. And if he bows alone, then shares with the imam in the two prostrations, his prayer is not invalidated. There is a distinction between this and the case where the imam bows and prostrates once and raises his head from it, then a man comes and enters with him and bows and prostrates twice, his prayer is invalid. The distinction is that in the first case, only an extra ruku' was introduced, because it was obligatory upon him to follow the imam in the two prostrations, and that does not invalidate the prayer. As for here, it involves introducing an extra rak'ah, namely ruku' and prostration. And if he catches the imam in the last sitting and does not sit with him, but stands and recites, what he does of standing and recitation before the imam finishes the tashahhud is not considered. As in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage addresses the fiqh of catching a rak'ah in congregational prayer. The primary rule, based on a statement of Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), is that a person catches the rak'ah if he bows (ruku') with the imam before the imam raises his head. If the imam raises his head before the follower bows, the rak'ah is lost. The commentary expands: catching the rak'ah is achieved either by sharing any part of the standing (qiyam) with the imam, or by sharing the ruku' (which has the legal status of standing). It is not necessary to have two separate takbirs (one for ihram and one for ruku'); a single takbir with intention suffices, though the intention for ruku' is void. A note (tanbih) follows: if the follower misses the ruku', he must still follow the imam in sujud (prostration), even though that sujud does not count as part of his prayer. He then makes up the missed rak'ah later. If he bows alone and then joins the imam in sujud, his prayer is valid because he only added an extra ruku', not a full rak'ah. This is distinguished from a case where someone enters after the imam has already prostrated once and tries to perform a full rak'ah (ruku' and two sujuds) by himself, which invalidates his prayer. Finally, if one catches the imam in the last sitting (tashahhud) and stands to pray without sitting, his recitation before the imam finishes is not considered. All rulings are sourced from al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid.

Key Terms
إدراك الركعة (idrak al-rak'ah): The act of joining the prayer in time to perform a full rak'ah with the imam, specifically by bowing (ruku') before the imam rises.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower who prays behind an imam in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Reciting at least one verse after the imam's recitation.
D) Making two separate takbirs.

Key Takeaway
To catch a rak'ah, the follower must either share part of the standing (qiyam) with the imam or perform ruku' before the imam raises his head.

Validity of a Follower's Premature Bowing (Rukū') Before the Imam
Explains validity conditions for a follower's premature rukū' with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a follower's bowing before the imam is valid in the Hanafi school, and apply the principle of participation (mushārakah) to evaluate validity.

Core Idea
Participation in part of the rukū' suffices for validity, but bowing before the imam's recitation is invalid.

In congregational prayer, a follower must follow the imam. What happens if the follower bows before the imam? The Hanafi school holds that if the imam has recited at least one verse and catches the follower in his bowing, the bowing is valid although disliked. This lesson unpacks the conditions, the principle of participation, and related scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the follower bowing before the imam. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh tanzih). Recognize the hukm level from the text: validity with karāhah.
Dislike does not affect validity; it only indicates the act is discouraged.
2
Locate the condition for validity
Two conditions are required: (a) the imam must have recited at least one verse before the follower bowed, (b) the imam must ‘catch’ the follower in his bowing, meaning the follower is still in rukū' when the imam reaches rukū'. Find these in the source.
The text says: 'after the imam recited what makes the prayer valid' and 'his imam catches him in it'.
3
Understand the principle of participation (mushārakah)
The follower's bowing is valid because he shares with the imam in part of the rukū'—either its beginning or its end. The commentator argues that just as sharing in the end suffices, sharing in the beginning also suffices. This is the core legal reasoning.
Hanafi fiqh uses this principle to allow limited participation; other schools may require full catch.
4
Distinguish the case of premature bowing before imam's recitation
If the follower bowed before the imam recited a verse, then even if the imam later catches him, the bowing is invalid because it was 'before its proper time'. This is a separate condition that overrides participation.
The text contrasts this with the valid scenario.
5
Note related scenarios and distinctions
The passage also covers: (a) if the follower misses rukū', he must still follow the imam in sujūd even if it doesn't count; (b) adding an extra rukū' alone (without sujūd) does not invalidate, but adding a full extra rak'ah (rukū' + sujūd) does; (c) one takbir with dual intention is permissible but the intention is nullified. Identify these in the text.
These distinctions are important for practical application in congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن ركع قبل إمامِهِ، بعد قراءة الإمام ما تجوز به الصَّلاةُ ، فأدركَهُ إمامُهُ فيه، صح . فكان الشرط لإدراك الركعة إما مشاركة الإمام في جزء من القيام - وإن لم يشاركه في الركوع - أو في جزء مما له حكم القيام، وهو الركوع وإن لم يشاركه في القيام، ولا يشترط الإتيان بتكبيرتين للإحرام والركوع خلافاً لبعضهم، ولو كبر قائماً ينوي بتلك التكبيرة الركوع والافتتاح جاز، ولغت نيته، كما في «الفتح». تنبيه: يجب على المقتدي إذا فاته الركوع متابعة الإمام في السجود، وإن لم يحسب لـه مـن الصلاة، وإن لم يتابعه ووقف حتى قام ثم تابعه في بقية الصلاة وقضى ما فاته من الركعات بـعـد فراغ الإمام تجوز صلاته؛ لأنه يصلي تلك الركعة الفائتة بسجدتيها، ولو ركع وحده، ثم شارك الإمام في السجدتين، لا تفسد صلاته فرق بين هذا وبين ما إذا ركع الإمام و وسجد سجدة ورفع رأسه عنها، فجاء رجل ودخل معه وركع وسجد سجدتين فسدت صلاته، والفرق أنَّ في المسألة الأولى لم يدخل فيها إلا زيادة ركوع، لأنه قد وجب عليه متابعة الإمام في السجدتين، وذا لا يفسد الصلاة، أما هاهنا وجه إدخال زيادة ركعة وهو الركوع والسجود، وإن أدرك الإمام في القعدة الأخيرة ولم يقعد معه، ولكن قام وقرأ فما وجد من القيام والقراءة قبل فراغ الإمام من التشهد لا يكون معتبراً، كذا في التجنيس والمزيد » ( وإن ركع) المقتدي قبل إمامه ) ، وكان ركوعه ( بعد قراءة الإمام ما) أي: شيئاً (تجوز به الصَّلاةُ) وهو آية فأدركَهُ إمامُهُ فيه ) أي : في ركوعه، (صح) ركوعه لوجود المشاركة، لأن للركوع طرفين طرف الابتداء وهو الأول وطرف الانتهاء، فكما صحت مع مخالفته في الانتهاء فكذا في الأول، إذ الشركة في أحدهما كافية للصحة مع الكراهة، لقوله : ( إِنَّمَا جُعِلَ الإمَامُ لِيُؤْتَمَّ بِهِ، فَلا تَخْتَلِفُوا عَلَيْهِ، فَإِذَا كَبَّرَ فَكَبِّرُوا، وَإِذَا رَكَعَ فَارْكَعُوا " الحديث، وقال : «أما يَخْشَى الَّذِي يَرْفَعُ رَأْسَهُ قَبْلَ الإِمَامِ أَنْ يُحَوِّلَ اللَّهُ رَأْسَهُ رَأْسَ حِمَارٍ " وقيدنا بكون ركوعــه بـعـد قراءة الإمام آية، إذ لو كان قبل أن يقرأ الإمام آية، ثم قرأ [ الإمام ] وركع، والمقتدي راكــع فأدركه في الركوع لا يجزئه عن الركوع؛ لأنه قبل أوانه، كذا في ( البحر» عن « الذخيرة»، انتهى. وإلا لا.
And if he bows before his imam, after the imam recited what makes the prayer valid, and his imam catches him in it, it is valid. So the condition for catching the rak'ah is either sharing with the imam in a part of the standing – even if he did not share in the bowing – or in a part which has the ruling of standing, which is bowing even if he did not share in the standing. And it is not required to perform two takbirs for the opening and bowing, contrary to some. And if he says the takbir while standing intending by that takbir both bowing and opening, it is permissible and his intention is nullified, as in al-Fath. Note: It is obligatory on the follower, if he misses the bowing, to follow the imam in the prostration, even if it is not counted for him from the prayer. And if he does not follow him and waits until he stands and then follows him in the rest of the prayer and makes up what he missed of rak'ahs after the imam finishes, his prayer is valid; because he prays that missed rak'ah with its two prostrations. And if he bows alone and then shares with the imam in the two prostrations, his prayer is not invalidated. There is a difference between this and the case where the imam bowed and prostrated one prostration and raised his head from it, and a man came and entered with him and bowed and prostrated two prostrations – his prayer is invalid. The difference is that in the first case he only introduced an extra bowing, because he was obliged to follow the imam in the two prostrations, and that does not invalidate the prayer. As for here, he introduced an extra rak'ah, which is bowing and prostration. And if he catches the imam in the last sitting and does not sit with him, but stands and recites, then what he does of standing and recitation before the imam finishes the tashahhud is not considered. Because bowing has two ends: the beginning end and the end, so just as it is valid with his opposition in the end, so too in the beginning, since sharing in one of them is sufficient for validity with dislike. Due to his saying: 'Indeed the imam is appointed to be followed, so do not differ from him. When he says takbir, say takbir; when he bows, bow' etc. And he said: 'Does not the one who raises his head before the imam fear that Allah will turn his head into the head of a donkey?' And we restricted it to his bowing being after the imam recited a verse, because if it was before the imam recited a verse, then the imam recited and bowed while the follower was in bowing and caught him in the bowing, it does not suffice for the bowing because it was before its time. So in al-Bahr from al-Dhakhirah. End. And if not, no.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from al-Hidayah explaining the conditions under which a follower's premature bowing (rukū') before the imam is valid. The base ruling states that if a follower bows before the imam after the imam has recited the minimum valid amount (a verse), and then the imam catches him in that bowing, the bowing is valid. The commentator expands on this, explaining that the key is participation (mushārakah) with the imam in any part of the bowing (either its beginning or end), or in the standing that has the same ruling as bowing. It is not required to have two separate takbirs; one takbir with dual intention is valid but cancels the intention. The commentator then adds a note about the follower who misses bowing: he must follow the imam in prostration even if that prostration is not counted for his missed rak'ah. He illustrates with a scenario where if someone merely adds an extra bowing (without prostration) by following the imam in prostration separately, it is not invalid, but if he adds a full extra rak'ah (bowing + two prostrations) before the imam, the prayer is invalid. The proof is the hadith forbidding differing from the imam and warning against raising the head before him. Finally, the condition is reiterated: the follower's bowing must occur after the imam has recited at least one verse; otherwise, the bowing is invalid because it is premature. This is a Zahir al-Riwayah ruling from Imam Muhammad's books.

Key Terms
المشاركة (al-mushārakah): Participation in the imam's action; here, sharing any part of the rukū' (beginning or end) suffices for validity.
الكراهة (al-karāhah): Dislike (tanzihī) meaning the act is valid but discouraged; here, bowing before the imam is disliked but not invalid.
قبل أوانه (qabla awānihi): Before its proper time; a bowing performed before the imam's recitation is invalid because it is premature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the minimum requirement for a follower's bowing (rukū') before the imam to be valid?
A) The follower must complete his bowing before the imam stands up.
B) The imam must have recited at least one verse before the follower bowed, and the imam must catch the follower in the bowing.
C) The follower must have intended the bowing separately from the opening takbir.
D) The follower must not have missed any part of the imam's recitation.

Key Takeaway
A follower's premature bowing is valid if the imam had recited a verse and catches him in it, because participation in part of the action suffices; otherwise it is invalid.

Leaving the Mosque After Adhan: Rulings and Exceptions
States the ruling and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving a mosque after the adhan and identify the exceptions that alter the ruling.

Core Idea
Leaving after adhan is disliked not forbidden; exceptions exist for valid needs and to avoid suspicion.

This lesson examines the ruling on leaving a mosque after the adhan has been called, a common situation for many Muslims. The Hanafi school considers it disliked (makruh tanzih) based on a hadith warning of hypocrisy, but allows clear exceptions. Understanding these exceptions helps avoid unnecessary hardship without falling into prohibited behavior.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its base ruling
The act is leaving the mosque after the adhan but before performing the obligatory prayer. The base ruling is dislike (karahah tanzihiyyah).
The ruling is based on the hadith cited in the passage.
2
Analyze the evidence (dalil)
The hadith says: 'None leaves the mosque after the call except a hypocrite, or a man who leaves for a need intending to return.' The exception for need indicates the ruling is not prohibition.
The hadith is ahad, so the ruling remains at the level of dislike, not obligation or prohibition.
3
List the exceptions
The text mentions several exceptions: (1) If one is an imam or muezzin for another congregation that would disperse without him; (2) According to al-Nihayah, leaving to pray in a neighborhood mosque is absolutely permissible; (3) If one has already prayed alone, leaving is allowed except at zuhr and 'isha when the congregation is being set up.
These exceptions show that the ruling is context-dependent.
4
Understand the zuhr/'isha exception
Leaving after praying alone is not disliked generally, but at zuhr and 'isha it becomes disliked to avoid suspicion of rejecting the congregation or being a heretic.
This is based on the principle of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking means to evil).
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a person who has already prayed alone after adhan and wants to leave the mosque at maghrib time. This is not disliked because maghrib is not one of the specified times. But if they leave at zuhr, it would be disliked.
The ruling is specific to the circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it is disliked for him to leave a mosque in which the adhan was called until he prays, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'None leaves the mosque after the call except a hypocrite, or a man who leaves for a need intending to return.' Except if he is establishing another congregation, such as being an imam or muezzin in another mosque whose people would disperse by his absence, because he is leaving the form of completing the meaning and the consideration is for the meaning. And in al-Nihayah: If he leaves to pray in his neighborhood mosque with the congregation, there is no problem absolutely, without restricting it to imam or muezzin, said al-Zayla'i. And al-Kamal said: The better is not to leave. End. And if he leaves after his prayer alone, it is not disliked for him to leave afterwards, because he responded to the call of Allah once, so it is not obligatory upon him a second time. Except that it is disliked for him to leave if the congregation is established before his leaving in the times of zuhr and 'isha; because although he responded to the caller, he is suspected of opposing the congregation openly, or perhaps it is thought that he does not consider praying behind the people of Sunnah valid, as the Kharijites and Shiites claim. And he said to him: 'Order whoever believes in Allah and the Day...'
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the sharh on the dislike (karāhah) of leaving the mosque after the adhan before performing the obligatory prayer. The commentator brings the hadith that only a hypocrite leaves after the call, except for a legitimate reason with intent to return. The general ruling is dislike (makruh tanzih), but there are exceptions: (1) if one is an imam or muezzin for another congregation that would disperse without him, it is allowed because the benefit (the communal prayer) outweighs the image of completing the form; (2) according to al-Nihayah, leaving to join another congregation in one's neighborhood is absolutely permissible, though al-Kamal considers it better not to leave. If one has already prayed alone, leaving is not disliked unless it is at zuhr or 'isha when the congregation is being set up, because it may cause suspicion of rejecting the congregation. The ruling is based on the hadith and the principle of avoiding suspicion. This is an established Hanafi ruling from the later authorities (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Key Terms
الكراهة (al-karāhah): Dislike; here it means the act is discouraged but not sinful (karahah tanzihiyyah).
التهمة (al-tuhmah): Suspicion; leaving at zuhr or 'isha may cause suspicion of hypocrisy or rejection of the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Zuhr and 'Isha
C) Zuhr and Asr
D) Maghrib and 'Isha

Key Takeaway
Leaving a mosque after adhan is disliked but not haram; exceptions include valid needs, leading another congregation, and after praying alone except at zuhr and 'isha.
