Prostration Before the Imam: General Validity and Abu Hanifa's Condition
Intra-Hanafi dispute on prostration timing with qiyas reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi ruling on a follower prostrating before the imam, explain Abu Hanifa's specific condition regarding the imam's rukū', and apply the principle of taba'iyyah (following) to determine validity in similar scenarios.

Core Idea
A follower's prostration before the imam is valid if caught, except when done before the imam raises from rukū' (Abu Hanifa).

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the follower's timing relative to the imam in prayer. While the general rule holds that a premature prostration is cured if the imam catches the follower, a reported view from Abu Hanifa imposes a stricter condition: if the prostration occurs before the imam has even risen from bowing, it remains invalid. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of the fundamental principle that the follower's actions are legally bound to the imam's sequence.

Guided Path
1
State the General Ruling
Identify the opening ruling: if a follower prostrates before the imam and the imam catches him in that prostration, it is valid. This is the default position.
2
Isolate Abu Hanifa's Condition
Note the exception reported from Abu Hanifa: if the prostration occurs before the imam raises his head from rukū', even if the imam later catches the follower, it does not count. The key is the timing relative to the imam's current posture.
3
Trace the Qiyas Argument
Understand the analogy: just as bowing before the imam's recitation of a verse invalidates the bowing (as mentioned later in the passage), so too prostration before the imam's rise from rukū' is invalid because it is premature in the imam's right. The follower's act is judged by the imam's state.
4
Apply to the Prolonged Prostration Scenario
Work through the case where the imam prolongs the first prostration and the follower mistakenly joins a second. The ruling depends on intention: following overrides personal intention unless the follower clearly intended a separate second prostration.
5
Summarize the Intra-Madhhab Difference
Conclude that Abu Hanifa's view is stricter on timing, creating a practical difference: some Hanafi scholars would require the follower to repeat the prostration if it fell before the imam's rise from rukū', while others would accept it if caught.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سجد قبل إمامه وأدركه فيه صح. وعن أبي حنيفة: أنه لو سجد قبل رفع الإمام من الركوع، ثم أدركه الإمام فيها، لا تجزئه؛ لأنه قبل أوانه في حق الإمام، فكذا في حقه؛ لأنه تبـع لــه، ولو أطـال الإمام في السجود فرفع المقتدي، فظن أنه سجد ثانية فسجد معه إن نوى بها الأولى أو لم تكن له نية، تكون عن الأولى، وكذا إن نوى الثانية والمتابعة ترجيحاً للمتابعة، وتلغو نية غيره للمخالفة، وإن نوى الثانية، لا غير كانت عن الثانية فإن أدركه الإمام فيها ،صحت وعلى قياس ما روي عن أبي حنيفة فيمن سجد قبل رفع الإمام من الركوع تجب أن لا تجوز لأنه سجد قبل أوانــه فـي حـق الإمام، فكذا في حقه لأنه تبع، كما في ( التبيين»، و «الفتح» وقدمنا ما إذا أتى بالركوع والسجود قبل الإمام، ( وإلا ) أي: وإن لم يدركه الإمام بأن رفع رأسه من الركوع، ثم ركع الإمام أو أدركه الإمام في الركوع، وكان ركوعه قبل قراءة الإمام آية (لا) يصح ركوعه ولـو شـاركه الإمـام فـيـه؛ لكونه قبل أوانه فيلزمه أن يركع بعد ركوع الإمام، وإذا لم يفعل وانصـرف مــن صلاته بطلـت.
And if he prostrates before his imam and his imam catches him in it, it is valid. And from Abu Hanifa: that if he prostrates before the imam raises from bowing, then the imam catches him in it, it does not suffice him; because it is before its time in the imam's right, so too in his right; because he is a follower. And if the imam prolongs the prostration and the follower raises, thinking that he prostrated a second time, and prostrates with him, if he intended the first or had no intention, it is for the first. Similarly if he intended the second and following, giving precedence to following, and his intention of other is nullified for opposition. And if he intended only the second, it is for the second; if the imam catches him in it, it is valid. And by analogy to what is reported from Abu Hanifa about one who prostrates before the imam raises from bowing, it must be that it is not valid because he prostrated before its time in the imam's right, so too in his right because he is a follower, as in al-Tabyin and al-Fath. And we have already mentioned when he performs bowing and prostration before the imam. And (if not) meaning if the imam does not catch him, such as he raised his head from bowing, then the imam bowed, or the imam caught him in the bowing, and his bowing was before the imam recited a verse, then his bowing is not valid even if the imam shared in it; because it was before its time, so he must bow after the imam's bowing, and if he does not do so and leaves his prayer, it becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on a follower who prostrates (sajdah) before the imam, followed by an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a specific condition. The general rule is that if the follower prostrates before the imam and the imam catches him in that prostration, it is valid. However, Abu Hanifa states that if the follower prostrates before the imam raises from rukū' (i.e., the imam is still in bowing), then even if the imam later catches him in that prostration, it is not valid because the prostration was prematurely done in relation to the imam, and the follower is legally bound to the imam's actions. The commentator then discusses a scenario where the imam prolongs the first prostration and the follower mistakenly thinks it is a second prostration and joins; the ruling depends on intention, giving precedence to following the imam (muwāfaqah). The passage concludes by linking back to the earlier ruling on bowing before the imam, reiterating that if the follower's bowing occurred before the imam recited a verse, it is invalid, even if the imam catches him, because it was prematurely performed. This is a relatively specific point within the broader topic of following the imam, and the authority from Abu Hanifa is cited as a report (riwāyah) from him.

Key Terms
السجود قبل الرفع من الركوع (al-sujūd qabla al-raf' min al-rukū'): Prostration performed before the imam raises his head from bowing; considered premature and invalid per Abu Hanifa.
تبِعَ (tabi'a): Follower; the legal status of being bound to the imam's actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When the follower prostrates before the imam completes his recitation.
C) When the follower prostrates after the imam has finished the prayer.
D) When the follower prostrates without the opening takbir.

Key Takeaway
A follower's prostration before the imam is generally valid if caught, but Abu Hanifa's reported view makes an exception when it occurs before the imam's rise from rukū', emphasizing strict temporal alignment with the imam.

Leaving the Mosque After Adhan – Ruling and Exceptions
Ruling on leaving mosque after adhan with proof and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the mosque after adhan, identify the exceptions, and apply the special rule for Zuhr and 'Isha to avoid suspicion.

Core Idea
Leaving after adhan is makruh, but excused for valid needs; in Zuhr/'Isha, join congregation as nafl to avoid suspicion.

This passage details the ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan before praying. The basic ruling is dislike (makruh), grounded in a hadith that only a hypocrite or one with a need intending to return leaves after the call. The text then elaborates exceptions for imams, mu'adhdhins, those who have already prayed, and a special case for Zuhr and 'Isha where leaving could create suspicion of opposing Ahl al-Sunnah. Learning these nuances prevents misunderstanding and helps apply the ruling correctly in varied situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Leaving the mosque after the adhan until one prays. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked).
Not haram, as exceptions exist.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith: 'None leaves the mosque after the call except a hypocrite, or a man who leaves for a need intending to return.' The wording implies blame for leaving without need.
Hadith is ahad, so zanni al-thubut, resulting in dislike rather than prohibition.
3
Trace the exceptions
The hadith itself exempts one with a need intending to return. The passage adds specific exceptions: imam or mu'adhdhin for another mosque, and one who has already prayed alone (except for Zuhr and 'Isha).
Intra-Hanafi differences exist on whether leaving for another mosque is allowed absolutely (al-Zayla'i) or only for imam/mu'adhdhin.
4
Analyze the special case of Zuhr and 'Isha
If a person prayed alone but the congregation is established before they leave, leaving is makruh because it invites suspicion of opposing Ahl al-Sunnah. The remedy is to join the congregation as nafl (supererogatory prayer).
This does not apply to Fajr, 'Asr, Maghrib due to timing issues for nafl.
5
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on Maghrib nafl
Zahir al-Riwayah prohibits joining the Maghrib congregation as nafl. Abu Yusuf allows it, with differing reports on whether to make taslim with the imam or complete four rak'ahs. The relied-upon position is to avoid it.
This shows how the school accommodates different views while preferring one.

Source Text

(وإنْ خرج بعد صلاتِهِ منفرداً لا يُكْرَهُ) له الخروج بعد، لأنه قد أجاب داعي الله مرة فلا يجب عليه ثانياً، (إلا) أنه يكره خروجه ( إذا أُقيمت الجماعةُ قبل خروجه في ) وقتي ( الظهر والعشاء)؛ لأنه وإن أجاب الداعي لكن يتهم لمخالفة الجماعة عياناً، أو ربما يُظن أنه لا يرى جواز الصلاة خلف أهل السنة كما يزعم الخوارج والشيعة. وقد قال له : « مر من كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر، فلا يَقِفن مواقف التهم »، كذا في (التبيين)، و (الدراية) (فيقتدي فيهما) أي: الظهر والعشاء (متنفّلا) لدفع التهمة عنه، وأما في غيرهما من الصلوات فيخرج بعد صلاته منفرداً، وإن أخذ المؤذن في الإقامة؛ لكراهية النفل بعد الفجر والعصر، ولزوم الكراهة في المغرب، إما بموافقة الإمام للتنفل بالبتيراء، وإما بمخالفته إن أتمَّ أربعاً، فإن مكث ولم يخرج في الظهر والعشاء بغير اقتدائه متنفلاً، كره لمخالفته الجماعة. وفي ظاهر الرواية: لا يتنفل مع الإمام في المغرب. وروي عن أبي يوسف: أنه يدخل معه ويسلم معه. وروي عنه أنه يتمها أربعاً بعد سلام الإمام؛ لأن مخالفة الإمام أهون من مخالفة السنة، لأنها مخالفة بعد الفراغ، ويصير كالمقيم إذا اقتدى بمسافر وكالمسبوق، وفي ( المحيط » : لو أضاف إليها ركعة أخرى يصير متنفلاً بأربع ركعات، وقد قعد على رأس الثالثة وهو مكروه، كذا في ( الدراية » ، وقال الكمال: لو سلم مع الإمام فعن بشر لا يلزمه شيء، وقيل: فسدت ويقضي أربعاً لأنه التزم بالاقتداء ثلاث ركعات فيلزمه أربع كما لو نذر ثلاثاً. انتهى.
It is disliked for him to leave a mosque in which the adhan has been given until he prays, because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'None leaves the mosque after the call except a hypocrite, or a man who leaves for a need intending to return.' (Except if he is establishing another congregation) by being an imam or mu'adhdhin in another mosque such that people would disperse in his absence, because he is leaving a form of completion for the meaning, and consideration is for the meaning. And in al-Nihaya: If he leaves to pray in the mosque of his quarter with the congregation, there is no harm absolutely, without the restriction of imam or mu'adhdhin, said al-Zayla'i. Al-Kamal said: The best is not to leave. End. (And if he leaves after having prayed alone, it is not disliked) for him to leave afterwards, because he has responded to the call of Allah once, so it is not obligatory upon him a second time. (Except) that his leaving is disliked (if the congregation is established before his departure) in the two times of Zuhr and 'Isha; because even though he responded to the caller, he is suspected of opposing the congregation openly, or perhaps it might be thought that he does not consider prayer behind Ahl al-Sunnah permissible, as the Khawarij and Shi'a claim. And it has been said to him: 'Command whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day to not stand in positions of suspicion.' So in al-Tabyin and al-Diraya: (he follows the imam in these two) i.e., Zuhr and 'Isha (as a supererogatory worshipper) to remove suspicion from himself. As for other prayers, he leaves after his solitary prayer, even if the mu'adhdhin begins the iqama, because of the dislike of supererogatory prayer after Fajr and 'Asr, and the necessity of dislike in Maghrib, either by agreeing with the imam in supererogatory prayer with the 'bitara' [prayer with three rak'ahs?], or by disagreeing if he completes four. If he stays and does not leave in Zuhr and 'Isha without following the imam as a supererogatory worshipper, it is disliked due to opposing the congregation. And in Zahir al-Riwaya: He does not perform supererogatory prayer with the imam in Maghrib. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf: He enters with him and makes taslim with him. And it is narrated from him that he completes it as four after the imam's taslim, because opposing the imam is easier than opposing the Sunnah, because it is opposition after completion, and he becomes like a resident who follows a traveler, and like a latecomer. And in al-Muhit: If he adds another rak'ah to it, he becomes a supererogatory worshipper with four rak'ahs, and he sat at the end of the third, which is disliked. So in al-Diraya. Al-Kamal said: If he makes taslim with the imam, according to Bishr nothing is incumbent upon him, and it was said: It is corrupted and he must make up four, because he committed himself by following to three rak'ahs, so four become incumbent upon him, just as if he vowed three. End.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on leaving a mosque after the adhan has been given, before performing the prayer. It begins by stating that leaving is disliked (makruh) based on a hadith that only a hypocrite or one with a need intending to return leaves after the call. Exceptions are then detailed: if the person is an imam or mu'adhdhin in another mosque whose absence would cause the congregation to disperse, leaving is permitted because the need to serve a broader religious purpose outweighs the form. Al-Zayla'i notes an absolute permission if one goes to pray in his local mosque. Al-Kamal says it is better not to leave. The passage then addresses a different scenario: if a person has already prayed alone (without congregation), it is not disliked to leave afterwards, because they have fulfilled the obligation. However, an exception is made for the two prayers of Zuhr and 'Isha: if the congregation is established before the person leaves, it becomes disliked to leave because it may arouse suspicion that they oppose congregational prayer or the Ahl al-Sunnah. To avoid this suspicion, the person should join the congregation as a supererogatory (nafl) worshipper. For other prayers (Fajr, 'Asr, Maghrib), leaving is allowed even if the iqama is given, because supererogatory prayer at those times is disliked (Fajr and 'Asr) or problematic (Maghrib). The passage then discusses the details of joining the Maghrib prayer as a supererogatory worshipper, including differences of opinion among Hanafi scholars: the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwaya) is that one should not enter with the imam for Maghrib nafl. Abu Yusuf allows entering and making taslim with the imam. Another narration from him says to complete four rak'ahs after the imam's taslim. Various opinions are cited about the validity and necessity of making up the prayer if one follows the imam in Maghrib nafl.

Key Terms
الخروج (al-khurūj): Leaving the mosque
كراهة (karāhah): Dislike (makruh tanzih)
الخوارج (al-khawārij): A sect that historically opposed the legitimate caliph and held extreme views, including rejection of prayer behind Ahl al-Sunnah.
متنفلاً (mutanafilan): Performing supererogatory (nafl) prayer; here it refers to joining the congregation with the intention of nafl to avoid suspicion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it specifically for Zuhr and 'Isha that a person who prayed alone must not leave if the congregation is established?
A) Because these prayers are longer.
B) To avoid suspicion of opposing Ahl al-Sunnah or the congregation.
C) Because nafl prayer is recommended at these times.
D) Because the hadith only applies to these times.

Key Takeaway
Leaving the mosque after adhan is makruh tanzih, but exceptions for imams/mu'adhdhins and those who have prayed alone exist, with a special rule for Zuhr and 'Isha requiring joining as nafl to avoid suspicion.

The Hanafi Interpretation of 'Do Not Pray a Similar Prayer After a Prayer'
Interpretation of the hadith 'Do not pray a similar prayer after a prayer'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi relied-upon interpretation of the hadith 'Do not pray a similar prayer after a prayer' and apply it to the ruling on repeating a fard congregation in the same mosque.

Core Idea
Repeating a fard congregation in the same mosque is makruh tahrimi, not to forbid nafl but to prevent waswasa and disorder.

This passage presents a hadith that seems to prohibit something, but its exact meaning was debated among early scholars. The Hanafi school, through al-Fath, settles on an interpretation that addresses practical concerns: preventing unnecessary repetition of congregations and protecting the worshipper from doubt. Understanding this interpretation clarifies why certain acts that appear similar are discouraged.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its literal prohibition
Read the hadith text: 'Do not pray a similar prayer after a prayer.' Notice it forbids something, but what exactly is 'similar'? The ambiguity requires interpretation.
The word 'similar' (مثلها) is key.
2
Survey the early interpretations
Al-Zayla'i reports three interpretations: (1) a prohibition on mixing recitation and silence in nafl; (2) a prohibition on immediately repeating a fard for extra reward; (3) a prohibition on repeating a prayer based on mere doubt. Each targets a different issue.
The first interpretation is attributed to 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud.
3
Identify the Hanafi relied-upon interpretation
The text states: 'It is interpreted as repeating the congregation in the mosque in the first manner, or as a prohibition of making up missed fard prayers for fear of defect.' This is from al-Fath. The Hanafi school takes this as the operative understanding.
The 'first manner' means in the same way as the original congregation.
4
Derive the ruling and its hukm level
Repeating a fard congregation in the same mosque is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). Making up missed prayers without necessity is also discouraged. The prohibition is not on all nafl but on problematic repetitions.
The underlying illa is prevention of waswasa and disorder.
5
Apply to a modern scenario
Consider a person who prays fajr in a mosque and then forms a second congregation for the same fajr prayer. According to the Hanafi school, this is makruh tahrimi and should be avoided.
Exceptions exist for missed prayers made up individually.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يُصلِّي بعد صلاةٍ مِثلَها) (1) هذا لفظ الحديث. قال الزيلعي واختلفوا في تفسيره فقيل: معناه لا يصلي ركعتان بقراءة وركعتان بغير قراءة، روي ذلك عن عمر وعلي وابن مسعود فيكون بياناً لفرض القراءة في ركعات النفل كلها، وقيل: كانوا يصلون الفريضة ثم يصلون بعدها مثلها، يطلبون بذلك زيادة الأجر فنهوا عن ذلك، وقيل: هو نهي عن إعادة المكتوبة بمجرد توهم من غير تحقيق؛ لما فيه من تسليط الوسوسة على القلب. انتهى. وهو محمول على تكرار الجماعة في المسجد على الهيئة الأولى، أو على النهي عن قضاء الفرائض مخافة الخلل في المؤدى، كذا في «الفتح» والله أعلم.
And do not pray a similar prayer after a prayer. This is the wording of the hadith. Al-Zayla'i said: They differed in its interpretation. It was said: Its meaning is that he should not pray two rak'ahs with recitation and two rak'ahs without recitation, narrated from 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud, thus it is an explanation of the obligation of recitation in all rak'ahs of nafl. And it was said: They used to pray the fard then pray a similar prayer after it, seeking thereby increased reward, so they were prohibited from that. And it was said: It is a prohibition of repeating the obligatory prayer merely out of delusion without verification, because of what it entails of instilling waswasa in the heart. End. And it is interpreted as repeating the congregation in the mosque in the first manner, or as a prohibition of making up missed fard prayers for fear of defect in the performed one, as in al-Fath. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage presents a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Do not pray a similar prayer after a prayer.' Al-Zayla'i reports multiple interpretations from early authorities. The first interpretation (from 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud) is that it means one should not pray two rak'ahs with recitation (e.g., a fard) followed by two rak'ahs without recitation (e.g., in a qada' or nafl?), making it a ruling that all rak'ahs of nafl must include recitation. The second interpretation is that people used to pray a fard prayer and then immediately pray another identical prayer (e.g., another fard or similar) seeking extra reward, and they were prohibited from doing so. The third interpretation is that it forbids repeating an obligatory prayer based on mere doubt without verification, because that leads to waswasa (whisperings of Shaytan). The passage then states the relied-upon understanding (muhammad) in al-Fath: the prohibition is about repeating the congregation in the mosque in the same manner (i.e., holding a second congregation for the same fard prayer in the same mosque), or it is a prohibition against making up missed fard prayers while already performing the current one, for fear of causing defect. The commentator concludes with 'Allah knows best'.

Key Terms
يؤدي (yu'addī): To perform an obligation; the 'performed' prayer is the one currently being offered.
وسوسة (waswasa): Whisperings from Shaytan that cause doubt and anxiety about acts of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the interpretation from al-Fath, what does the hadith 'Do not pray a similar prayer after a prayer' primarily prohibit?
A) Praying any nafl after a fard.
B) Repeating the same congregation for a fard prayer in the mosque.
C) Making up missed prayers without recitation.
D) Praying two rak'ahs with recitation after two without recitation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school interprets the hadith as a prohibition on repeating a fard congregation in the same mosque, not on all nafl prayers, to prevent waswasa and disorder.

Joining the Congregation as a Nafl Worshipper After Dhuhr and Isha
Fiqh ruling with intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for joining the imam as a supererogatory worshipper after performing the obligatory prayer for each prayer time, and identify the relied-upon position regarding Maghrib.

Core Idea
Joining the imam as a nafl worshipper after fard is recommended in Dhuhr and Isha to avoid suspicion, but disliked in Maghrib.

When a person has already performed the obligatory prayer individually, and another congregation is in progress, should he join as a follower? The Hanafi school distinguishes between prayer times. This lesson unpacks the ruling, including a difference of opinion within the school on Maghrib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer times
The passage specifies rulings for Dhuhr, Isha, Fajr, Asr, and Maghrib. Note which are mentioned directly.
The matn mentions Dhuhr and Isha; the commentary extends to other times.
2
State the ruling for Dhuhr and Isha
For these two prayers, the person should join the congregation as a mutanaffil (nafl worshipper) to avoid suspicion of neglecting worship.
This is mustahab.
3
Note the exceptions for Fajr and Asr
After Fajr and Asr, supererogatory prayer is disliked (makruh), so the person should leave the mosque alone, even if the iqamah is given.
Nafl after these two is always disliked, regardless.
4
Examine the Maghrib dispute
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, it is disliked to join. Abu Yusuf has two narrations allowing it, either by finishing with the imam (3 rak'ahs) or by completing 4. Understand the reasoning for each.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Zahir al-Riwayah view: do not join.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
The text presents the Zahir al-Riwayah as the primary position, and later scholars (like al-Kamal) discuss details, but the disliked status remains the operative ruling for fatwa.
Authority: Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He follows [the imam] in both as a supererogatory worshipper. And do not pray after a prayer its like. ... (He follows in both) meaning Zuhr and 'Isha (as a supererogatory worshipper) to ward off suspicion from him. As for other prayers, he exits after his prayer alone, even if the mu'adhdhin has begun the iqamah, because of the dislike of supererogatory prayer after Fajr and 'Asr, and the necessity of dislike in Maghrib, either by agreeing with the imam for supererogatory prayer with the three-rak'ah prayer or by disagreeing if he completes four. If he stays and does not exit in Zuhr and 'Isha without following him as a supererogatory worshipper, it is disliked due to his contradicting the congregation. In the apparent transmission: He does not perform supererogatory prayer with the imam in Maghrib. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he enters with him and finishes with him. It is also narrated from him that he completes it as four after the imam's salam, because contradicting the imam is easier than contradicting the sunnah, as it is contradiction after completion, and he becomes like a resident who follows a traveler and like a latecomer. In al-Muhit: If he adds another rak'ah, he becomes a supererogatory worshipper of four rak'ahs, and he sat after the third, which is disliked. Al-Kamal said: If he says salam with the imam, according to Bishr nothing is incumbent upon him, and it is said: his prayer is invalidated and he must pray four because he committed by following to three rak'ahs, so four are incumbent upon him as if he vowed three. End. 'Do not pray after a prayer its like' – this is the wording of the hadith. Al-Zayla'i said: They differed in its interpretation. It is said: Its meaning is do not pray two rak'ahs with recitation and two without recitation, narrated from 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud, thus it is a clarification of the obligation of recitation in all supererogatory rak'ahs. It is said: They used to pray the obligatory prayer then pray its like after it, seeking additional reward, so they were prohibited from that. It is said: It is a prohibition of repeating the obligatory prayer due to mere suspecting without verification, because of the authority it gives to whispering in the heart. End. It is interpreted as repeating the congregation in the mosque in the first manner, or as a prohibition of making up obligatory prayers for fear of defect in the one performed, as in al-Fath. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on two matn statements from Nur al-Idah. The first statement deals with following the imam in congregational prayer after having already performed the obligatory prayer. The commentator explains that for Zuhr and 'Isha, a person who missed the first congregation should join the imam as a supererogatory (nafl) worshipper to avoid suspicion of being disengaged from worship. For Fajr and 'Asr, nafl after the obligatory prayer is disliked (makruh), so he should leave separately. For Maghrib, the ruling differs: according to the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), he should not perform nafl with the imam, but Abu Yusuf narrates two positions: either he joins and finishes with the imam (three rak'ahs) or he completes four after the imam's salam. The text discusses the reasoning and concludes with the disliked nature of certain options. The second matn quotes the hadith 'Do not pray after a prayer its like.' The commentator presents three interpretations: (1) it means do not pray two rak'ahs with recitation and two without, emphasizing recitation in all nafl; (2) people used to pray fard then pray a similar nafl for extra reward; (3) it prohibits repeating the same obligatory prayer unnecessarily. The relied-upon interpretation is that it refers to repeating the same congregation in the mosque with the same appearance, or to avoid causing suspicion about the validity of the performed prayer.

Key Terms
متنفلا (mutanafifilan): One who prays as a supererogatory (nafl) worshipper, not as an obligatory prayer.
التهمة (al-tuhmah): Suspicion or accusation, here referring to the suspicion that one is neglecting worship.
البتراء (al-batira'): A three-rak'ah prayer, referring to the nafl performed after Maghrib in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah), what is the ruling for performing supererogatory prayer with the imam in Maghrib?
A) Recommended (mustahab)
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Obligatory (wajib)
D) Permissible (mubah)

Key Takeaway
Joining the congregation as a nafl worshipper after performing the fard is recommended for Dhuhr and Isha, but disliked for Maghrib per the relied-upon position.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
7 min
Interpreting the Hadith 'Do Not Pray After a Prayer Its Like'
Hadith interpretation and application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain three interpretations of the hadith 'لا يُصلِّي بعد صلاةٍ مِثلَها' and identify which interpretation the Hanafi school relies upon for its ruling.

Core Idea
The hadith does not prohibit all nafl after fard; it is specifically about repeating the same congregation or causing suspicion about the validity of the performed prayer.

The hadith 'Do not pray after a prayer its like' is a well-known narration. Its meaning has been debated among scholars. This lesson explores three interpretations and concludes with the one adopted in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Quote the hadith and note its chain
The hadith is 'لا يُصلِّي بعد صلاةٍ مِثلَها'. It is reported by al-Zayla'i in Nasb al-Rayah. The chain is ahad, so its proof value is zanni.
The hadith is not mutawatir.
2
Present the first interpretation
Some scholars (including 'Umar, 'Ali, Ibn Mas'ud) interpret it as a prohibition of praying two rak'ahs with recitation and two without, meaning recitation is required in all nafl rak'ahs.
This interpretation makes it a clarification of the obligation of qira'ah in nafl.
3
Present the second interpretation
Others say people used to pray fard then pray its like (same number) for extra reward, and they were prohibited from that to avoid innovation.
This interpretation treats it as a prohibition of excessive nafl.
4
Present the third interpretation
A third group says it prohibits repeating the obligatory prayer (qada') due to mere doubt, as it could lead to waswasa.
This interpretation is about avoiding psychological harm.
5
State the Hanafi preferred interpretation
The text in al-Fath says it is interpreted as (1) repeating the congregation in the mosque in the first manner (i.e., the same appearance), or (2) a prohibition of making up fard prayers for fear of defect in the one performed.
The Hanafi school leans toward the first, regarding it as disliked to repeat the same congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

It is said: They used to pray the obligatory prayer then pray its like after it, seeking additional reward, so they were prohibited from that. It is said: It is a prohibition of repeating the obligatory prayer due to mere suspecting without verification, because of the authority it gives to whispering in the heart. End. It is interpreted as repeating the congregation in the mosque in the first manner, or as a prohibition of making up obligatory prayers for fear of defect in the one performed, as in al-Fath. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on two matn statements from Nur al-Idah. The first statement deals with following the imam in congregational prayer after having already performed the obligatory prayer. The commentator explains that for Zuhr and 'Isha, a person who missed the first congregation should join the imam as a supererogatory (nafl) worshipper to avoid suspicion of being disengaged from worship. For Fajr and 'Asr, nafl after the obligatory prayer is disliked (makruh), so he should leave separately. For Maghrib, the ruling differs: according to the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), he should not perform nafl with the imam, but Abu Yusuf narrates two positions: either he joins and finishes with the imam (three rak'ahs) or he completes four after the imam's salam. The text discusses the reasoning and concludes with the disliked nature of certain options. The second matn quotes the hadith 'Do not pray after a prayer its like.' The commentator presents three interpretations: (1) it means do not pray two rak'ahs with recitation and two without, emphasizing recitation in all nafl; (2) people used to pray fard then pray a similar nafl for extra reward; (3) it prohibits repeating the same obligatory prayer unnecessarily. The relied-upon interpretation is that it refers to repeating the same congregation in the mosque with the same appearance, or to avoid causing suspicion about the validity of the performed prayer.

Key Terms
مثلها (mithlaha): A prayer similar in form and structure to the one just performed.
تفسير (tafsir): Interpretation or explanation, here of the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the interpretations of the hadith 'لا يُصلِّي بعد صلاةٍ مِثلَها' mentioned in the passage?
A) Prohibition of praying two rak'ahs with recitation and two without
B) Prohibition of praying a nafl with the same number of rak'ahs as the fard
C) Prohibition of repeating the obligatory prayer out of mere doubt
D) Prohibition of all nafl prayers after any fard

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'لا يُصلِّي بعد صلاةٍ مِثلَها' is interpreted by the Hanafi school to prohibit repeating the same congregation or making up fard without reason, not all nafl prayers.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Sajdah al-Sahw: Its Obligation and Conditions
Introduces the chapter on prostration of forgetfulness, defines sahw, and establishes its obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-sahw (wajib), list its conditions, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib to compensate for a forgotten wajib, analogous to dam in Hajj.

The prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) is a critical element of prayer that compensates for unintentional omissions. This lesson examines its legal status, the dispute over whether it is wajib or sunnah, and the conditions that trigger it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause (sahw) and its definition
The author explains that sahw (heedlessness) is the cause for sajdah, distinguished from nisyan (forgetfulness). Note that sahw may occur without awareness.
This sets the foundation for when sajdah al-sahw becomes relevant.
2
List the conditions for sajdah al-sahw
The passage specifies four conditions: the omitted element must be wajib, performance within prayer conditions, not saying salam while remembering a rukn, and no occurrence of a building preventer (e.g., deficient time).
These conditions are essential for the obligation to arise.
3
Analyze the evidence for obligation (wajib)
The author argues that sajdah al-sahw is wajib because it is a guarantee for a missing wajib, and such guarantees are obligatory. He draws an analogy (qiyas) to dam (blood sacrifice) in Hajj.
This is the main proof (talil) for the Hanafi position.
4
Evaluate the opposing view (sunnah) and its refutation
Some scholars (based on Imam Muhammad) consider it sunnah, citing that returning to sajdah does not invalidate tashahhud. The response clarifies that 'tashahhud' means sitting, and returning to omitted wajibs does invalidate the sitting, as per rulings on intentional speech.
The dispute turns on the interpretation of Imam Muhammad's statement.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequences
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that sajdah al-sahw is wajib, as affirmed by the majority (Sarakhsi, Halwani). If wajib, one must perform it when a wajib is omitted; if sunnah, it is optional.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) affects the worshipper's obligation.

Chapter of the Prostration of Forgetfulness. When [the author] mentioned the obligatory and supererogatory [prayers], he began to explain the compensator for deficiency that can occur in both. The addition of 'prostration' to 'forgetfulness' is of the type of adding a ruling to its cause, and that is the origin in addition, as in al-Dirayah, because addition is for specification, and the strongest type of specification is the specification of the effect by the cause, as in al-Mustasfa. The principle is that when a thing is added to a thing, the addendum becomes a cause for the thing added, unless evidence indicates otherwise, like Zakat al-Fitr and Hajj al-Islam, as in al-'Inayah. There is no difference in language between forgetfulness (nisyan) and sahw, as in al-Tahrir. End. And sahw is heedlessness. He said in al-Misbah: They distinguished between it and forgetfulness, in that the forgetful person remembers when reminded, while the sahw person is not. He said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: Forgetfulness is the disappearance of a thing from the mind after its presence, while sahw may be concerning something one knows or does not know. As in al-Bahr. The discussion of this chapter is in aspects: First, the cause, which you know is sahw. Second, its interpretation, which you also know. Third, its condition, which is that the omitted [element] must be wajib, the performance of the prostration with the conditions of prayer, that one does not say salam while remembering a rukn, and that nothing occurs that prevents building upon the prayer, including the arrival of a deficient time. It is not a condition that one intentionally says the salam. Fourth, its ruling, which is compensation for deficiency, enraging the devil, and pleasing the Most Merciful. Fifth, its quantity and integral (rukn), which is two prostrations. Sixth, its form, which is tashahhud and taslim. Seventh, its preferred place, which is after salam. Eighth, its legal status, which is obligation (wujub). He then began to explain it, saying: (It is obligatory) because it is a guarantee for what is missing, and a guarantee for what is missing cannot be other than obligatory, especially when the missing thing is characterized by obligation, and it is legislated to compensate for a deficiency that occurs in the worship, so it is obligatory, like the blood [sacrifices] in Hajj. Some said it is sunnah, deducing from what Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: that returning to sajdah al-sahw does not invalidate tashahhud, as if he meant the sitting. They said: if it were obligatory, it would have invalidated it like the prostration of tilawah and the prostration of the second [sajdah]? This is said by al-Zayla'i. And in al-Bada'i' he added: meaning reading tashahhud, so he said: returning to these omitted things, namely the prostration of the second, the prostration of tilawah, and reading tashahhud, invalidates tashahhud, meaning it invalidates the sitting, so he used tashahhud to mean sitting, as Muhammad intended by his statement: 'even if he speaks, laughs, or breaks his wudu intentionally, his prayer is invalidated because it is an intentional salam while there remains a rukn of the prayer.' End. This mention in al-Bada'i' of the invalidation of the sitting by reading tashahhud is the statement of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi and al-Halwani. And he said in al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Dhakhira: If he omits recitation...
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage initiates the chapter on Sajdah al-Sahw, the prostration of forgetfulness, which compensates for deficiencies in prayer. The author first explains the linguistic and legal relationship between 'sajdah' (prostration) and 'sahw' (forgetfulness): the ruling is attributed to its cause, a standard principle in Hanafi usul. He distinguishes sahw from nisyan (forgetfulness), noting that while both involve a lapse, sahw may occur without awareness, whereas a forgetful person can be reminded. The discussion is organized into eight aspects: (1) the cause (sahw), (2) its definition, (3) its conditions, (4) its ruling (compensation), (5) its quantity (two sajdas), (6) its form (tashahhud and taslim), (7) its preferred time (after salam), and (8) its legal status (wajib). The main contention is whether sajdah al-sahw is obligatory (wajib) or sunnah. The author asserts obligation (yajib), arguing that it is a guarantee for a missing obligatory element, similar to the blood sacrifices in Hajj. Those who consider it sunnah cite a statement of Imam Muhammad that returning to sajdah al-sahw does not invalidate the tashahhud, implying it is not obligatory. The response clarifies that the tashahhud here means the sitting (qa'dah), and that returning to omitted wajibs does invalidate the sitting, as indicated by related rulings. The preferred position is that sajdah al-sahw is wajib.

Key Terms
السهو (al-sahw): Heedlessness or lapse of attention; may be from something known or unknown.
النسيان (al-nisyan): Forgetfulness, the disappearance of something from the mind after it was present; the person can be reminded.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation; a ruling that requires performance and omission incurs sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is sunnah
B) It is wajib
C) It is fard
D) It is mubah

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib to compensate for a forgotten wajib in prayer, and its conditions must be met for the obligation to arise.

Ruling and Proof of Sajdah al-Sahw
Establishes wajib ruling of sajdah al-sahw with definitions, conditions, and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-sahw, explain its conditions, and derive its wajib status from textual and analogical proofs.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-sahw is wajib because it compensates a missed obligatory act, like dam in Hajj.

In this passage, the author of Imdad al-Fattah explains the chapter on sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). He begins by defining key terms, enumerating eight aspects of the prostration, and then defends the position that it is wajib (obligatory) with textual and analogical evidence. The passage also addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether sajdah al-sahw raises the tashahhud, concluding with the correct relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being discussed? What is the ruling (hukm) according to the passage? The passage states that sajdah al-sahw is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith: 'For every forgetfulness there are two prostrations after the salutation' and the practice of the Companions.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah, and the practice is reported in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The imperative 'fal-yasjud' indicates wujub according to the Hanafi principle that a command indicates obligation unless contraindicated.
The hadith also mentions 'after the salutation', which indicates the preferred timing but does not affect the obligation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement within the Hanafi school? Some Hanafi scholars (following Imam Muhammad's report) consider it sunnah, arguing that returning to sajdah al-sahw does not raise the tashahhud.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The author states that the correct view is that it is wajib, because it does raise the tashahhud (its recitation) and the salam. The sitting is not raised because it is a stronger fard.
This tarjih is supported by majority Hanafi authorities and the practice of the Salaf.

Chapter of Sajdah al-Sahw. When he mentioned the obligatory and supererogatory prayers, he began to explain the compensator for deficiency that can occur in them. Adding 'sajdah' to 'sahw' is of the type of adding the ruling to the cause, and that is the principle in addition, as in al-Dirayah; because addition is for specification, and the strongest aspect of specification is the specification of the effect by the cause, as in al-Mustasfa. The principle is that when something is added to something, the addendum is the cause of the added, unless evidence indicates otherwise, like Zakat al-Fitr and Hajj of Islam, as in al-Inayah. There is no difference in language between forgetfulness (nisyan) and inadvertence (sahw), as in al-Tahrir. End. And sahw is heedlessness. He said in al-Misbah: They differentiated between it and nisyan, in that the forgetful person, if you remind him, remembers, whereas the inadvertent is not like that. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: Nisyan is the departure of a thing from the soul after its presence, while sahw can be about something one knows or does not know, as in al-Bahr. The discussion on this chapter has several aspects: first, the cause—and you know it is sahw; second, its interpretation—and you know it; third, its condition: that the omitted act is wajib, performing the prostration with the conditions of prayer, that he does not salute while remembering a rukn, and that nothing occurs that prevents building upon the prayer, including the onset of a deficient time. It is not a condition that he intends to salute. Fourth, its ruling: it compensates the deficiency, enrages the devil, and pleases the Merciful. Fifth, its quantity and rukn: two prostrations. Sixth, its form: tashahhud and taslim. Seventh, its preferred place: after the salutation. Eighth, its description: wujub. Then he began to explain it, saying: 'It is obligatory' because it is a guarantee for what is missed, and a guarantee for what is missed is only obligatory, especially if the missed act is described as obligatory, and it is legislated to compensate a deficiency that occurred in worship, so it is obligatory, like the blood offerings (dimā') in Hajj. Some said it is sunnah, arguing from what Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: that returning to sajdah al-sahw does not raise the tashahhud, meaning the sitting. They said: if it were obligatory, it would raise it like the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah) and the original prostration (sajdat al-salbiyyah). This is what al-Zayla'i said, and al-Bada'i added: that is, reciting the tashahhud. Then he said: Returning to these omitted acts—i.e., the original prostration, the prostration of recitation, and reciting the tashahhud—raises the tashahhud, meaning it raises the sitting. This is the statement of Shams al-Aimmah al-Sarakhsi and al-Halwani. And in al-Tatarakhaniyya from al-Dhakhira: If he inadvertently omitted reciting the tashahhud until he saluted, but he sat for the duration of the tashahhud, then he remembered and returned to recite the tashahhud, then exited the prayer before completing the recitation of the tashahhud, his prayer is not invalid. He said: I found a text narration that returning to reciting the tashahhud does not raise the sitting, and that is the statement of Zufar. From Abu Yusuf there are two narrations. Shams al-Aimmah al-Halwani and Shams al-Aimmah al-Sarakhsi mentioned that it raises the sitting, just as it is raised when returning to the prostration of recitation and the original prostration, to the extent that if he speaks after beginning to recite the tashahhud before completing it, his prayer becomes invalid. Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl mentioned in his Fatawa that the sitting is not raised, and in Waqi'at al-Natifi the fatwa is on this. End. Similar in al-Tajnis and al-Mazid: there is a difference in tarjih regarding the raising of the sitting by reciting the tashahhud after having omitted it inadvertently and having sat for the duration of the tashahhud. End. The correct is the first, i.e., the obligation of sajdah al-sahw, for what we mentioned, and therefore it raises the tashahhud, i.e., its recitation, such that if he salutes immediately upon raising his head from the two prostrations of forgetfulness, his prayer is valid, and he becomes one who has omitted a wajib. Likewise, it raises the salutation. If it were not wajib, it would not raise them. It does not raise the sitting because it is stronger than it, being a fard, unlike the original prostration because it is stronger than the sitting due to being a rukn, and the sitting is for concluding the pillars; and unlike the prostration of recitation because it is an effect of recitation which is a rukn, so it is given its ruling. It was said that the prostration of recitation does not raise the sitting because it is wajib, so it does not raise the fard, and Shams al-Aimmah chose that, but the first is more correct, and it is the chosen view and the more correct of the two narrations, as in al-Tabyin, al-Fath, and al-Tatarakhaniyya. And his statement (two prostrations) is the subject of 'yajib' because of his statement: 'For every forgetfulness there are two prostrations after the salutation' and he said: 'Whoever doubts in his prayer, let him prostrate two prostrations after he salutes.' Narrated by Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah, and because he prostrated two prostrations for forgetfulness while sitting after the taslim, as in al-Bukhari and Muslim, and acted upon by Umar ibn al-Khattab, Ali, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Ammar ibn Yasir, Abdullah ibn Abbas, Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr, Anas ibn Malik, and from the Tabi'in: al-Hasan, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla, al-Thawri, al-Hasan ibn Salih, the people of Kufa, and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, as in al-Burhan (with tashahhud and taslim) for what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the chapter of Sajdah al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) from the matn of Nur al-Idah. The author begins by explaining the terminology: 'sajdah' is added to 'sahw' because the forgetfulness is the cause for the prostration, a standard linguistic principle in Hanafi usul. He clarifies that in language, 'sahw' and 'nisyan' are synonymous, though some differentiate: the forgetful person can be reminded, while the inadvertent cannot. The passage then enumerates seven aspects: the cause (sahw), its interpretation, condition (the omitted act must be wajib, etc.), ruling (compensation for deficiency), quantity (two sajdahs), form (tashahhud and taslim), and preferred place (after salam). The eighth aspect is the description of the ruling itself: wujub (obligation). The matn then states 'yajib' (it is obligatory). The commentary defends this wajib status with reasoning: it is a guarantee (daman) for a missed obligatory act, analogous to blood offerings (dimā') in Hajj. It then addresses an opposing view that it is sunnah, based on a report from Imam Muhammad that returning to sajdah al-sahw does not invalidate the tashahhud (sitting). The author refutes this by noting that if it were only sunnah, it would not raise the tashahhud, but the majority of Hanafi scholars (including Shams al-Aimmah) hold that it does raise it. A lengthy discussion ensues about whether returning to recite the tashahhud after forgetting it raises the sitting (qa'dah). Various opinions are cited: Zufar says it does not; Abu Yusuf has two narrations; al-Sarakhsi and al-Halwani say it does; Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl says it does not. The author concludes that the correct view is that it does raise the tashahhud (recitation) and the salam, but not the sitting itself because the sitting is a fard (obligatory pillar) and stronger than a wajib. The prostration of recitation and the original prostration are stronger because they are arkan (pillars), hence they raise the sitting. The author then quotes hadith from Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, Bukhari, and Muslim to prove that sajdah al-sahw is two prostrations after salam, and cites the practice of numerous Companions and early scholars. Thus the relied-upon position is that sajdah al-sahw is wajib.

Key Terms
سهو (sahw): Forgetfulness or inadvertence in prayer, the cause for the prostration.
نسيان (nisyan): Forgetfulness, the departure of something from the mind after its presence.
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for errors in prayer.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act that is established by zanni evidence, distinct from fard.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act; omission does not require compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi position, what is the ruling of sajdah al-sahw?
A) It is fard.
B) It is wajib.
C) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-sahw is wajib in the Hanafi school, required to compensate for any missed wajib act in prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Sujud al-Sahw: Obligation, Components, and the Qa'dah Dispute
Explains the obligation and components of Sujud al-Sahw with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the components of Sujud al-Sahw according to the Hanafi school and explain why the qa'dah is not nullified by returning to tashahhud.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Sahw is wajib with tashahhud and taslim; the qa'dah is a fard that cannot be nullified by a wajib.

Sujud al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) is a key mechanism in Hanafi prayer to repair deficiencies caused by forgetful omission of a wajib. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah outlines its obligatory nature, its required components, and a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about whether returning to recite tashahhud after having sat for it nullifies the earlier sitting. Understanding this ruling clarifies when the prayer remains valid and when it becomes invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is the hukm level (fard/wajib)?
The text explicitly states 'سجدتان بتشهد وتسليم' (two prostrations with tashahhud and taslim) as wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited for the obligation? Identify the hadith and its transmitters.
The hadith 'لِكُلِّ سَهْوِ سَجْدَتَانِ بَعْدَ السَّلامِ' is reported by Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, Bukhari, and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove obligation? What is the legal link?
The imperative form implies obligation, but Hanafi usul categorizes it as wajib (not fard) due to zanni evidence.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
What is the dispute about returning to tashahhud after having sat? State the two views.
Zufar, and some narrations from Abu Yusuf, say it nullifies the qa'dah; the relied-upon view says it does not.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which view is correct and why? What is the operative ruling (mufta bihi)?
The correct view is that the qa'dah is not nullified because it is a fard (stronger) and tashahhud is a wajib (weaker).

يرفــع القعدة وهو قول زفر. وعن أبي يوسف روايتان وذكر شمس الأئمة ( الحلواني» وشمس الأئمة السرخسي : أنه يرفض القعدة، كما ترفض إذا عاد إلى سجدة التلاوة والصلبية، حتى لو تكلـم بعد شروعه في قراءة التشهد القعدة بقراءة التشهد بعدما كان تركه ساهياً وقعد قدر التشهد. انتهى. والصحيح الأول، وهـو : وجوب سجود السهو، لمـا ذكـرنـا ولهذا يـرفــع التشهد أي قراءته حتى لو سلم بمجرد رفعـه مـن سجدتي السهو صحت صلاته، ويـكـون تـاركـاً للواجب، وكذا يرفع السلام ولولا أنه واجب لما رفعهما، وإنما لا يرفع القعدة لأنها أقوى منه لكونها فرضاً، بخلاف السجدة الصلبية لأنها أقوى من القعدة؛ لكونها ركناً والقعدة لختم الأركان، وبخلاف سجدة التلاوة؛ لأنها أثر القراءة وهي ركن فيعطى لها حكمها، وقيل: إن سجدة التلاوة لا ترفع القعدة لأنها واجبة، فلا ترفع الفرض، واختاره شمس الأئمة والأول أصح، وهو المختار وهـو أصح الروايتين، كما في « التبيين » و « الفتح»، و « التاتارخانية»، وقوله (سجدتان) فـاعـل يـجـب لقوله : « لَكُلِّ سَهْوِ سَجْدَتَانِ بَعْدَ السَّلامِ » ) وقال : «مَنْ شَكٍّ فِي صَلَاتِهِ فَلْيَسْجُدْ سَجْدَتَانِ بَعْدَمَا يُسَلَّمْ ) رواه أبو داود وابن ماجه وه لأنَّهُ سَجَدَ سَجدَتَيْنِ لِلْسَهُو وَهُوَ جَالِسٌ بَعْدَ التسليم » (۳) كما في ( البخاري »، و «مسلم»، وعمل به عمر بن الخطاب، وعلي، وسـعـد بـن أبـي وقاص، وعبد الله بن مسعود، وعمار بن ياسر وعبد الله بن عباس، وعبد الله بن الزبير، وأنـس بـن مالك، ومن التابعين الحسن، وإبراهيم النخعي، وعبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى، والثوري، والحسن ابن صالح، وأهل الكوفة، وعمر بن عبد العزيز ، كما في ( البرهان» (بتشهد وتسليم) لما ذكرنا لِتَرْكِ واجب سهواً وإن تكرر. من أن سجود السهو يرفع التشهد والسلام، فيجب إعادتهما، ويأتي فيه بالصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والدعــاء كما اختاره الكرخي، وقال فخر الإسلام أنه اختار عامة أهل النظر من مشايخنا، وهو المختار عندنا وذكر «قاضي خان» و « ظهير الدين أن الأحوط الإتيان بذلك فيه وفيما ،قبله، واختاره « الطحاوي» وقيل: عندهما يصلي في الأولى ويدعو ، لكون سلامه يخرجه موقوفاً فهي قعدة ختم، وفي « المـفـيـد » : وهـو الأصح، وعند محمد: لا يخرجه فيؤخرهما إلى قعدة السهو الأخيرة، كذا في شرح المقدسي ». فإن قلت: المروي ( أَنَّهُ سَلَّمَ ثُمَّ سَجَدَ سَجْدَتِين ثُمَّ سَلَّمَ ) ولم يذكر فيه التشهد ؟! قلت: التسليم دال عليه؛ لأنه ذكر التسليم في الحديث وأريد به بعد التشهد لما روى الكمال: ( أنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى العَصْرَ فَسَلَّمَ مِنْ ثَلاثٍ إِلَى أَنْ قَالَ: فَصَلَّى رَكْعَةً، ثُمَّ سَلَّمَ ثُمَّ سَجَدَ سَجْدَتَيْنِ ثُمَّ سَلَّمَ " انتهى. ولم يكن سلامه الأول والثاني إلا بعد التشهد فكذا الثالث، فقد أطلق التسليم وأريد بكونه بعد التشهد، (لِتَرْكِ واجب) لا سنة، لأنه لجبر نقصان، والصلاة لا توصف بالنقصان على الإطلاق بترك سنة، فلا يحتاج إلى الجابر، وأما الفرض ففواته يفوت به الأصل لا الوصف فلا ينجبر بغيره، ولأن الأقوى لا ينجبر بالأدنى، وقولنا بترك واجب، كما قال « القاضي الإمام صدر الإسلام» وجوبه بشيء واحد وهو ترك الواجب. قال في التاتارخانية » : وهذا أجمع مما قاله أكثر المشايخ على أن سجود السهو يجب بستة أشياء: بتقديم ركن، وتأخير ركن، وبتكرار ركن، وبتغيير واجب، وبترك واجب، وبترك سنة تضاف إلى جميع الصلوات، نحو أن يترك التشهد في القعدة الأولى، فإن الوجوه الستة تخرج على هذا، فالتقديم والتأخير فيه ترك واجب مراعاة الترتيب وتكرار الركن فيه تأخير الذي بعده وتقديمه واجب، والجهر والإسرار في غير محله فيه تغيير واجب، والأصح أن القعود الأول واجب، وعليه المحققون، فقولنا لترك واجب شامل يغني عن الخمسة المتروكة ( سهواً)، لما روينا ولأن الساهي معذور فيستحق التخفيف بـجـبـر الخلل بالسجود، والمتعمد لا يستحق إلا بالتغليظ، وهو بإعادة كل صلاته لجبر نقصها، وقوله (وإن تكرر) واصل بما قبله وهذا بالإجماع، فليس عليه إلا سجدتان فقط للسهو المتكرر وقولـه عـلـيـه الصـلاة والسلام: « لِكُلِّ سَهْوِ سَجْدَتَانِ بَعْدَ السَّلامِ ، " محمول على شمول الأشخاص أو الصلاة،
Two prostrations with tashahhud and taslim. The tashahhud until he says salam, but he sat for the measure of tashahhud, then remembered and returned to reciting tashahhud, then exited the prayer before completing the recitation of tashahhud, his prayer is not invalidated. He said: I found a narration explicitly that returning to the recitation of tashahhud does not nullify the sitting, and it is the view of Zufar. From Abu Yusuf there are two narrations, and Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned that it nullifies the sitting, just as it is nullified if one returns to a sajdah of tilawah or the spinal sajdah, so much so that if he spoke after beginning to recite tashahhud before completing it, his prayer is invalid. Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl mentioned in his Fatawa that it does not nullify the sitting, and in Waqi'at al-Natifi the fatwa is on this. End. And similar is in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid, and the weighting differed concerning the nullification of the sitting by the recitation of tashahhud after having left it forgetfully and sat for the measure of tashahhud. End. And the correct is the first, namely: the obligation of sajdat al-sahw, for what we mentioned, and for this reason it nullifies the tashahhud, i.e., its recitation, so that if he says salam immediately after rising from the two sajdat al-sahw, his prayer is valid, and he becomes one who left a wajib. Likewise, it nullifies the salam, and were it not wajib, it would not nullify them. It does not nullify the sitting because it is stronger than it, being a fard, contrary to the spinal sajdah because it is stronger than the sitting, as it is a rukn, and the sitting is for the seal of the arkan. And contrary to the sajdah of tilawah, because it is an effect of the recitation which is a rukn, so it is given its ruling. And it was said: The sajdah of tilawah does not nullify the sitting because it is wajib, so it does not nullify the fard, and Shams al-A'imma chose this, but the first is more correct, and it is the chosen view, and it is the more authentic of the two narrations, as in al-Tabyin, al-Fath, and al-Tatarkhaniyya. And his statement (two prostrations) is the subject of 'it is obligatory' because of his statement: 'For every forgetfulness, two prostrations after the salam.' And he said: 'Whoever doubts in his prayer, let him prostrate two prostrations after he says salam.' Reported by Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah, and because he prostrated two prostrations for forgetfulness while sitting after the taslim, as in al-Bukhari and Muslim, and acted upon by Umar ibn al-Khattab, Ali, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Ammar ibn Yasir, Abdullah ibn Abbas, Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr, Anas ibn Malik, and from the tabi'un: al-Hasan, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla, al-Thawri, al-Hasan ibn Salih, the people of Kufa, and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, as in al-Burhan. (With tashahhud and taslim) for what we mentioned for the leaving of a wajib forgetfully, even if repeated. That Sujud al-Sahw nullifies the tashahhud and the salam, so they must be repeated, and in it one comes with the salat upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, and du'a as chosen by al-Karkhi. Fakhr al-Islam said that the generality of the people of insight among our shaykhs chose it, and it is the chosen view according to us. Qadi Khan and Zahir al-Din mentioned that the precaution is to do that in it and in what preceded it, and al-Tahawi chose it. And it was said: According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he prays in the first and makes du'a, because his salam exits him suspended, so it is a sitting of seal. In al-Mufid it is the most correct. And according to Muhammad, it does not exit him, so he delays them to the last sitting of forgetfulness, as in Sharh al-Maqdisi. If you say: It is reported that 'He said salam, then prostrated two prostrations, then said salam' and he did not mention tashahhud. I say: The salam indicates it; because he mentioned salam in the hadith and intended by it after tashahhud, as al-Kamal narrated: 'The Prophet prayed Asr and said salam from three rakahs' until he said: 'He prayed a rakah, then said salam, then prostrated two prostrations, then said salam.' End. His first and second salam were not but after tashahhud, so likewise the third. He mentioned salam absolutely and intended it to be after tashahhud. (For leaving a wajib) not a sunnah, because it is to repair a deficiency, and prayer is not described as having deficiency at all by leaving a sunnah, so it does not need a repair. As for fard, its omission loses the essence not the attribute, so it cannot be repaired by another. And because the stronger cannot be repaired by the weaker. And our statement 'for leaving a wajib' is as Qadi Imam Sadr al-Islam said: Its obligation is due to one thing, which is leaving the wajib. Al-Tatarkhaniyya said: This is more comprehensive than what most scholars said that Sujud al-Sahw is obligatory due to six things: the advancement of a rukn, the delay of a rukn, the repetition of a rukn, the alteration of a wajib, the leaving of a wajib, and the leaving of a sunnah that pertains to all prayers, such as leaving tashahhud in the first sitting. For the six aspects reduce to this: advancement and delay involve leaving the wajib of observing order; repetition of a rukn involves delaying the one after it and advancing it, which is wajib; vocalization and silence in the wrong place involves altering a wajib. The most correct is that the first sitting is wajib, and the verifiers are upon this. So our statement 'for leaving a wajib' is comprehensive, sufficing for the five aspects left (forgetfully), because we have narrated and because the one who forgets is excused, so he deserves leniency by repairing the defect with prostration, while the intentional one deserves only severity, which is repeating his entire prayer to repair its deficiency. And his statement ('even if repeated') is connected to what precedes, and this is by consensus: he only needs two prostrations only for repeated forgetfulness. And his statement, peace be upon him, 'For every forgetfulness, two prostrations after the salam' is understood as encompassing persons or prayers.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, addresses the rulings of Sujud al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). It begins by establishing that Sujud al-Sahw consists of two prostrations accompanied by tashahhud (the testimony) and taslim (salutation). The author then discusses a scenario: someone forgets the tashahhud, sits briefly, then remembers and returns to recite it, but exits the prayer before completing it. The ruling is that the prayer remains valid. This leads into a dispute among Hanafi scholars: Zufar holds that returning to tashahhud nullifies the earlier sitting (qa'dah), while the relied-upon view (as per al-Natifi's fatwa and the choice of many scholars) is that it does not. The reason is that the sitting (qa'dah) is a fard (obligatory element), which is stronger than the tashahhud (a wajib). A wajib cannot nullify a fard. The passage then explains that Sujud al-Sahw nullifies the tashahhud and salam (meaning they must be repeated), but not the sitting itself. This is because the sitting is a fard. The text provides proofs from hadith: 'For every forgetfulness, two prostrations after the salam' and 'Whoever doubts in his prayer, let him prostrate two prostrations after he says salam.' These are reported by Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, Bukhari, and Muslim, and acted upon by many companions. The passage then discusses the nature of Sujud al-Sahw: it is wajib for leaving a wajib, not for leaving a sunnah or fard. Multiple forgetfulness requires only one set of two prostrations. The author argues that all six causes of Sujud al-Sahw mentioned by earlier scholars reduce to one: leaving a wajib. This simplification is comprehensive and eliminates redundancy. The passage also addresses whether tashahhud in Sujud al-Sahw includes salat upon the Prophet and du'a, noting that the recommended view is to include them. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each point with its dalil and internal Hanafi ikhtilaf, always returning to the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
سجدتا السهو (sajdatā al-sahw): The two prostrations performed to compensate for mistakes (forgetfulness) in the prayer.
القعدة (al-qa'dah): The sitting in prayer, specifically here the sitting after the prostration of forgetfulness or the initial sitting for tashahhud.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith in prayer, required in Sujud al-Sahw.
الواجب (al-wājib): An obligatory act that is between fard and sunnah; established by zanni evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum requirement for Sujud al-Sahw according to the Hanafi school?
A) Two prostrations only, without any recitation.
B) Two prostrations with tashahhud and taslim.
C) Two prostrations with only taslim, no tashahhud.
D) One prostration with tashahhud.

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-Sahw is wajib, consists of two prostrations with tashahhud and taslim, and the qa'dah (sitting) is a fard that cannot be nullified by returning to tashahhud.

Intentional Omission of a Wajib in Salah: No Sajda al-Sahw
Ruling on intentional omission of wajib acts and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for intentional omission of a wajib act in salah and identify the three weak exceptions for sajda al-sahw.

Core Idea
Intentional omission of a wajib requires i'ada, not sajda al-sahw; the three exceptions are weak.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: sajda al-sahw is only for forgetfulness. Intentional omission of a wajib is a sin and requires repeating the prayer. The author then mentions a weak opinion about three cases. Let's analyse the rule and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is intentional omission of a wajib in salah. The ruling: the person sins (i'thm) and must repeat the prayer (i'ada); no sajda al-sahw.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites ijma' (consensus) that reciting three short verses after al-Fatiha is wajib, establishing that wajib acts are binding and their intentional omission requires i'ada.
Dalil is from consensus, not explicit Quran or hadith.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Sajda al-sahw is legislated as a compensation for forgetfulness. Intentional omission is stronger, so sajda cannot compensate; only i'ada can remedy the deficiency.
The reasoning is based on the nature of sajda al-sahw as a lightening for forgetfulness.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a weak opinion (قيل) that sajda al-sahw is still required in three cases even if intentional: leaving the first sitting, delaying a prostration, and deep thought causing omission of a rukn.
The commentator uses 'قيل' to indicate doubt, showing this is not the relied-upon view.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi is that no sajda al-sahw is performed for any intentional omission; the three exceptions are dismissed as weak. The commentator does not adopt them.
Authority weight is from later fatawa works; the weak opinion is not from Zahir al-Riwayah.

And if he intentionally omits it, he sins, and repeating the prayer is obligatory, without its deficiency, and he does not prostrate for forgetfulness in the case of intentional [omission]; it is said except in three: leaving the first sitting, or delaying a prostration from the first rak‘ah until the end of the prayer, and his deliberate deep thought until it occupied him from a pillar, acting upon the word 'every', and it is not carried to include forgetfulness lest it abandon consensus, thus in al-Mustasfa. And it is necessary to mention some of the wajibs even if previously mentioned: if he leaves al-Fatiha, or most of it, or repeats it in any prayer, or part of it before reciting the sura; but reciting al-Fatiha a second time after reciting the sura does not necessitate sajda al-sahw because it is like adding a sura to the sura; similarly if he recites the sura after al-Fatiha in the last two rak‘ahs of the obligatory prayer, sajda al-sahw is not required in the chosen view because al-Fatiha alone is not specified in them, and recitation is better than silence, thus in al-Tajnis. And he prostrates for forgetfulness if he begins a letter, i.e., a verse of a sura, then remembers reciting al-Fatiha, or recites a verse while bowing or prostrating, or during the standing or sitting before reciting the tashahhud, or leaves part of the tashahhud even if little in the apparent riwaya because it is structured remembrance, so leaving part is like leaving all; or he recites tashahhud while standing between al-Fatiha and the sura; and if he recites the tashahhud before al-Fatiha, sajda al-sahw is not required in the sahih view, as in al-Diraya; or he delays the standing for the third [rak‘ah] immediately after finishing the first tashahhud, even if he remains silent, or adds to it to the extent of performing a pillar, whether with salawat upon the Prophet or otherwise, by istihsan due to delaying the wajib of standing, not because of the salawat itself nor because of the uttered dhikr of others, like repeating the tashahhud, or leaving one takbir of the ‘Id takbirs, or the takbir of bowing in the second rak‘ah of ‘Id, or the takbir of qunut because they are like the takbir of ‘Id; and it is said not required. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Dhahiriyya: there is no transmission for this; or if the imam lowers his voice in a place of jahr, or he or the individual raises [his voice] to the extent that the prayer is valid in the most sahih view, or he does not recite after al-Fatiha in the first two rak‘ahs three short verses or one long verse because reciting al-Fatiha with three short verses is wajib by consensus, as in al-Tajnis and al-Mazid, and with this is refuted what is said: the apparent meaning in al-Tabyin suggests that if he adds two short verses, no sajda is upon him because the majority has the ruling of the whole. End. When you have known from consensus the obligation of three with al-Fatiha, and if he intentionally leaves something of the wajib acts, he sins, and he does not prostrate for forgetfulness because it is legislated as a lightening for one who forgets, and this intentional [doer] must repeat the prayer as a strictness upon him to compensate its deficiency, for he cannot compensate it except by repeating, so it becomes a completion, and the obligation fell with the first, and it is said that the second is the obligation so it is the remover. And he does not prostrate in the intentional omission for forgetfulness because sajda al-sahw is known as a compensator for what is missed forgetfully legally, and the intentional is stronger so sajda al-sahw does not substitute for it, and because the intentional deserves strictness by repetition. Then he showed the weakness of the opinion of prostration for intentional omission with the expression of doubt in our saying: 'it is said except in three' cases: the first: leaving the first sitting intentionally; the second: delaying a prostration from the first rak‘ah intentionally until the end of the prayer; the third: his deliberate deep thought until it occupied him from the amount of a pillar.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on intentionally omitting a wajib act in salah. The base ruling is: if one intentionally omits any wajib, he commits a sin (أَيْمَ), must repeat the prayer (إعادة), and does not perform sajda al-sahw, because sajda al-sahw is only for forgetfulness, not for intentional acts. However, there is a weak opinion (قيل) that sajda al-sahw is still done in three specific cases even if the omission was intentional: (1) leaving the first sitting (القعود الأول), (2) delaying a prostration from the first rak'ah to the end of the prayer, and (3) being so deeply engaged in thought that one misses a rukn. The commentator then lists numerous situations that do require sajda al-sahw (due to forgetfulness), such as omitting part of al-Fatiha, reciting a verse in the wrong posture, or delaying the standing for the third rak'ah. This list illustrates the breadth of wajib acts and the specific conditions for sajda al-sahw. The passage concludes by reaffirming the main rule and clarifying that the three exceptions are weak (مضعف). The authority weight is from the later works (Fatawa) since the commentator is citing various sources like al-Mustasfa, al-Tajnis, al-Diraya, etc.

Key Terms
السهو (al-sahw): Forgetfulness that occurs unintentionally during prayer, for which sajda al-sahw is prescribed.
العمد (al-‘amd): Intentional action, knowing the ruling; this nullifies the forgetfulness ruling and requires repetition.
الواجبات (al-wājibāt): Obligatory acts of prayer that are not fard but wajib; intentional omission requires i'ada; forgetfulness requires sajda al-sahw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone intentionally omits the first sitting (tashahhud) in prayer, what is the correct Hanafi ruling?
A) He performs sajda al-sahw only, and the prayer is valid.
B) He must repeat the prayer and does not perform sajda al-sahw.
C) He does sajda al-sahw and repeats the prayer.
D) The prayer is invalid and no compensation is possible.

Key Takeaway
Intentionally omitting a wajib in salah requires i'ada, not sajda al-sahw; the three exceptions are weak and not relied upon.

Time of Sajda al-Sahw and Number of Taslims
Ruling on timing of sajda al-sahw and number of taslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the timing of sajda al-sahw (after salam) and the number of taslims (one to the right), and explain the rational and scriptural basis for these rulings.

Core Idea
Sajda al-sahw is sunnah after salam; one taslim to the right suffices.

This lesson examines two connected aspects of sajda al-sahw: its timing and the number of taslims. The Hanafi school, based on the hadith of Thawban and the principle that salam is an original wajib, holds that sajda al-sahw is performed after the final salam. For the taslims, the relied-upon view is that one taslim to the right is sufficient, as it achieves the exit from prayer. The passage also discusses the Shafi'i view on timing and internal Hanafi variations on the number of taslims, with a clear tarjih provided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
Note that the passage addresses two distinct but related rulings: when sajda al-sahw is performed (before or after salam) and how many taslims are given after it.
These are independent but often discussed together in fiqh texts.
2
Extract the Hanafi primary ruling
State the Hanafi position: sajda al-sahw is sunnah after salam, and one taslim to the right is sufficient (mufta bihi).
The passage explicitly mentions 'zahir al-riwaya' and 'mufta bihi'.
3
Analyze the proofs
For timing: the hadith of Thawban ('For every forgetfulness, two prostrations after the salam') and the principle that salam is an original wajib that takes precedence. For taslims: the first salam achieves tahlil (exit from prayer), so a second is not needed.
The Shafi'i school uses other hadiths to support before salam.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
The Shafi'i school holds sajda al-sahw before salam. Internally, some Hanafis prefer two taslims, but the majority and the commentator adopt one taslim as more precautionary.
The tarjih is based on multiple sources: al-Diraya, al-Muhit, al-Ikhtiyar.

قال فخر الإسلام ليسلم تلقاء وجهه ولا ينحرف عن القبلة، فيكون [ فرقاً ] بين سلام القطع وسلام السهو، وفي ( المحيط » : وعلى قول عامة المشايخ يكتفي بتسليمة واحدة وهو الأضمن للاحتياط ، كذا في ( الدراية» وفي «خواهر زاده»: لا يأتي بسجود السهو بعد تسليمتين لأن ذلك بمنزلة الكلام، وقوله ( في الأصح): يجوز أن يتعلق بتسليمة قال في « الدراية » ، عن «المجتبى » : وهو الأصح ، وهو قول العامة كما ذكرناه، ويجوز أن يتعلق بقولنا عن يمينه لما قال في مجمع الروايات » : ويسلم عن يمينه وهو الأصح. وقيل في الجانبين، وقيل: تلقاء وجهه فرقاً بين سلام القطع وسلام السهو، كما ذكرنا وفي ( الهداية» : ويأتي بتسليمتين هـو الصحيح،
