Standing After Final Tashahhud: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof on standing after final tashahhud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for standing after the final tashahhud and explain the sunnah of giving salam while sitting.

Core Idea
If you stand after final tashahhud, return and give salam sitting; the prayer remains valid.

This lesson addresses a common forgetfulness during prayer: after completing the final tashahhud, a person mistakenly stands up and may even perform an extra rak'ah. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance on how to rectify this situation while preserving the validity of the obligatory prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the situation: the person has performed the final sitting (julūs akhir) and then stood up, either inadvertently or deliberately, and possibly performed an additional rak'ah by reciting and bowing.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that he must return to sitting and give salam without repeating the tashahhud. Giving salam while sitting is sunnah; doing so standing is not invalid but abandons the sunnah.
The sunnah is to give salam while sitting.
3
Cite the proof
The proof is the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood up for a fifth rak'ah, was reminded by the companions' glorification, returned, gave salam, and performed sajda sahw.
Dalil: 'لأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم قام إلى الخامسة فسبح له فعاد وسلم وسجد للسهو'
4
Explain the consequence of adding an extra rak'ah
If he prostrates for the extra rak'ah, his obligatory prayer is not invalidated because the final sitting was already performed. He may recommendably tie another rak'ah to the extra one to make a two-rak'ah nafl.
The extra rak'ah can become a voluntary prayer by adding a second rak'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(وإن قعد) الجلوس (الأخير) قدر التشهد (ثم قام) وقرأ وركع (عاد) للجلوس؛ لأن ما دون الركعة بمحل الرفض، وسلّم) والعود للتسليم جالساً سنة؛ لأن السنة التسليم جالساً، والتسليم حالة القيام غير مشروع في الصلاة المطلقة بلا عذر، فيأتي به على الوجه المشروع «لأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم قام إلى الخامسة فسبح له فعاد وسلم وسجد للسهو» ولو سلم قائماً لم تفسد صلاته، وإن كان تاركاً للسنة، لأن السنة التسليم جالساً. من غير إعادة التشهد) وكذا لو قام عامداً يعود للتسليم ولا يعيد التشهد، وقال الناطفي: يعيده، وإن لم يعد ومضى في النافلة، فالصحيح عن علمائنا أن القوم لا يتبعونه لأنه لا اتباع في البدعة، لكنهم ينتظرونه قعوداً، فإن عاد قبل أن يقيد الخامسة بالسجدة اتبعوه في السلام، وإن قيد سلموا في الحال كذا في (الدراية) و(الفتح) (فإن سجد) للزائدة (لم يبطل فرضه) لوجود الجلوس الأخير في محله، ولم يترك إلا إصابة لفظ السلام، وهي ليست بفرض عندنا، وضم) استحباباً (إليها) أي: الزائدة ركعة (أخرى) في المختار إن شاء التصير الزائدتان له نافلة، ولا تنوب عن سنة الفرض على الصحيح؛ لأن المواظبة عليها بتحريمة مبتدأة، كما في (الهداية). ولا كراهة في الضم فيما بعد الفجر والعصر، كباقي الأوقات، إذ لا نقصان في الشروع في النفل على قول محمد، وهو المختار للفتوى، خلافاً لأبي يوسف، وكذا لو تنفل آخر الليل، فلما صلى ركعة طلع الفجر يتمه شفعاً بلا كراهة، ثم يصلي سنة الفجر، وإنما قيدنا الضم بالاستحباب، لأنهم اختلفوا في الضم من غير وقت مكروه، قيل: بالوجوب وقيل: وسجد للسهو. وسجد للسهو لتأخير السلام، وتمكن النقصان في الفرض بالخروج لا على الوجه الواجب.
And if he sits the final sitting, then stands, he returns and gives salam without repeating the tashahhud; and if he prostrates it does not invalidate his obligatory prayer, and he ties another rak'ah to it so that the two extra become supererogatory for him. (And if he sits) the final sitting, the amount of tashahhud, (then stands) and recites and bows, (he returns) to sitting; because what is less than a rak'ah is subject to abandonment, and (gives salam). Returning to give salam while sitting is sunnah; because the sunnah is to give salam sitting, and giving salam in a standing state is not legislated in absolute prayer without excuse, so he performs it in the prescribed manner. 'Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood up for the fifth, so they glorified him, so he returned and gave salam and prostrated for forgetfulness.' And if he gave salam while standing, his prayer would not be invalidated, although he would be abandoning the sunnah, because the sunnah is giving salam sitting. Without repeating the tashahhud. Similarly, if he stood deliberately, he returns for salam and does not repeat the tashahhud; al-Natafi said: he repeats it. And if he does not return and continues in supererogatory prayer, the correct position of our scholars is that the congregation does not follow him because there is no following in innovation, but they wait sitting. If he returns before tying the fifth with a prostration, they follow him in salam; if he ties, they immediately give salam, as in (al-Diraya) and (al-Fath). (If he prostrates) for the extra (rak'ah), (his obligatory prayer is not invalidated) because the final sitting occurred in its place, and only the pronunciation of salam was omitted, which is not obligatory according to us. And he ties (recommendedly) to it, i.e., the extra rak'ah, another (rak'ah) in the chosen view if he wishes so that the two extras become supererogatory for him, and they do not substitute for the sunnah of the obligatory prayer on the correct view; because the adherence to it is with an initial takbir, as in (al-Hidaya). And there is no dislike in tying after Fajr and Asr, like other times, since there is no deficiency in starting supererogatory prayer according to Muhammad, and it is the chosen view for fatwa, contrary to Abu Yusuf. Similarly, if one performs supererogatory prayer at the end of the night, and when he completes a rak'ah dawn appears, he completes it as pairs without dislike, then prays the sunnah of Fajr. And we only restricted tying to recommendation because they differed concerning tying outside a disliked time: some said obligatory, and some said: and he prostrates for forgetfulness. And he prostrates for forgetfulness due to delaying the salam, because a deficiency occurred in the obligatory prayer by exiting in a way other than the required manner.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with both hadith proof and rational reasoning. It discusses the scenario where after performing the final tashahhud, a person mistakenly stands up (thinking the prayer is not yet complete) and then recites and bows. The ruling is that he should return to the sitting position and give salam without repeating the tashahhud. The sunnah is to give salam while sitting; doing so standing is not invalid but contrary to sunnah. A hadith is cited where the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood for a fifth rak'ah, was reminded by the companions' tasbih, returned, gave salam, and performed sajda sahw. If the person adds an extra rak'ah (by prostrating after the second sajdah of the extra rak'ah), his obligatory prayer remains valid because the final sitting was already done properly; only the salam was delayed, which is not a pillar. Then he may recommendably tie another rak'ah to the extra one, making them a two-rak'ah nafl prayer. However, this nafl does not fulfill the sunnah of Fajr because it was begun with a separate takbir for the nafl. The passage also clarifies that tying extra rak'ahs after Fajr and Asr is not disliked, as per Imam Muhammad's view which is chosen for fatwa, unlike Abu Yusuf's view. Additionally, tying extra rak'ahs is recommended, not obligatory, and if one delays the salam due to the extra rak'ah, he should perform sajda sahw for the delay.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The sitting recitation of the testimony of faith in the final sitting.
الجلوس الأخير (al-julūs al-akhir): The final sitting of the obligatory prayer where tashahhud is recited.
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness performed to compensate for certain omissions or additions in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if after the final tashahhud a person stands up and performs an extra rak'ah (with prostration), what is the status of his obligatory prayer?
A) It becomes invalid.
B) It is valid but he must repeat the tashahhud.
C) It is valid and he may recommendably add another rak'ah to make it a nafl.
D) It is valid only if he intended nafl from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
Standing after final tashahhud does not invalidate the prayer; the sunnah is to return and give salam sitting.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Tying Extra Rak'ahs After Fajr and Asr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tying extra rak'ahs after Fajr/Asr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding tying extra rak'ahs after Fajr and Asr, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
According to Imam Muhammad, there is no dislike in tying extra rak'ahs after Fajr or Asr; this is the chosen view for fatwa.

This lesson examines an internal Hanafi difference concerning the permissibility of adding extra rak'ahs to an obligator prayer after it has been inadvertently prolonged by an extra unit. Specifically, does the time of day matter? Imam Muhammad holds no dislike, while Abu Yusuf had a different view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ikhtilaf
Recognize that the dispute is about whether it is disliked (makruh) to tie an extra rak'ah (to make two nafl) after Fajr and Asr prayers, when an extra rak'ah was added inadvertently.
2
State each position
Imam Muhammad holds that there is no dislike (la kirahah) in tying after Fajr and Asr, just like other times. Abu Yusuf holds there is dislike.
The text also mentions a general ikhtilaf about tying outside a disliked time: some said obligatory, some said voluntary.
3
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is Imam Muhammad's view, as stated in the text: 'wa huwa al-mukhtar lil-fatwa' (and it is the chosen view for fatwa).
This is the operative position for fatwa today.

Sajda Sahw in Voluntary Prayer and Building Another Pair
Ruling on building after sajda sahw in voluntary prayer with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building another pair of rak'ahs after sajda sahw in voluntary prayer and identify the exception for a traveler.

Core Idea
Building another pair after sajda sahw invalidates the first sajda; it must be repeated.

The passage addresses a common scenario in voluntary prayers: after performing prostration of forgetfulness, can one add another pair of rak'ahs? The Hanafi school considers it discouraged, and if done, the original sajda sahw becomes invalid, requiring repetition. An exception is made for a traveler who intends to settle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the person did: performed sajda sahw in a two-rak'ah voluntary prayer. The question: can he build another pair upon it? The ruling: it is discouraged (makruh tanzih) to build. If he builds, the first sajda sahw is invalidated and must be repeated.
2
Distinguish the two opinions
There is an intra-Hanafi disagreement. Abu Bakr al-A'mash and Abu Ja'far hold that the original sajda sahw is valid even if building occurs, so no repetition is needed. The majority view (al-Mukhtar, al-Fath) holds that the building invalidates the first sajda, so repetition is necessary. The latter is the mufta bihi position.
The text says 'فالأصح أن يعيده' (the most correct view is that he repeats it).
3
Apply the exception for a traveler
The text restricts the ruling to voluntary prayer. For a traveler who performs sajda sahw and then intends to settle (i.e., becomes a resident), building is allowed because otherwise his entire prayer would become invalid due to the change in travel status. However, even in this case, he must repeat the sajda sahw.
This exception is from al-Hidaya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سجد للسَّهو في شفع التطوع لم يبن شفعا آخر عليه استحبابا، فإن بني أعاد سجود السهو، في المختار. وقيل: لا يعيده لأنه وقع جابرا حين وقع فيعتد به عند أبي بكر الأعمش، وبه أخذ الفقيه أبو جعفر، كذا في الفتاوى الصغرى، فالأصح أن يعيده لبطلان الأول بما طرأ من البناء، كما في الفتح. وقيدنا بالنفل؛ لأن المسافر إذا سجد للسهو ثم نوى الإقامة فإنه يبني؛ لأنه لو لم يبن يبطل جميع صلاته، كذا في الهداية، ويعيد سجود السهو لبطلان الأول بالبناء.
And if one performs prostration of forgetfulness in a pair of voluntary prayer, he does not build another pair upon it, recommendedly. If he builds, he repeats the prostration of forgetfulness, in the chosen view. And it is said: he does not repeat it because it occurred as a compensator when it occurred, so it is considered valid according to Abi Bakr al-A'mash, and the jurist Abu Ja'far adopted that, as in al-Fatawa al-Sughra. So the most correct view is that he repeats it because the first is invalidated by what supervened from building, as in al-Fath. And we restricted it to voluntary prayer; because if a traveler performs prostration of forgetfulness and then intends to settle, he does build; because if he does not build, his entire prayer becomes invalid, as in al-Hidaya, and he repeats the prostration of forgetfulness because the first is invalidated by the building.
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that discusses a specific situation in voluntary prayer (nafl). If a person is praying a two-rak'ah voluntary prayer (shaf') and during it he performs sajda sahw (e.g., due to forgetfulness), he should not, after completing the prayer, build another two-rak'ah pair upon that sajda sahw. The recommended view is that he should not build; but if he does build (meaning he starts another pair of rak'ahs with the intention of joining it to the first pair), then he must repeat the sajda sahw because the first sajda is invalidated by the new building. There is an alternative opinion from Abi Bakr al-A'mash and Abu Ja'far that the original sajda sahw remains valid even if he builds, but the text declares the first view as 'most correct' (الأصح). The passage adds an exception: if a traveler (musafir) who has performed sajda sahw then intends to settle (i.e., becomes a resident), he may build upon his prayer because otherwise his entire prayer would become invalid due to the change in travel status. In that case, he must also repeat the sajda sahw due to the building.

Key Terms
شفع التطوع (shaf' al-tatawwu'): A pair of rak'ahs in voluntary prayer, usually two rak'ahs prayed together with one salam.
البناء (al-binā'): To join another pair of rak'ahs to the previous pair, treating them as one continuous prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view in this passage, if a person performs sajda sahw in a voluntary prayer and then builds another pair upon it, what must he do?
A) He must repeat the entire prayer.
B) He must repeat the sajda sahw only.
C) He does not need to do anything; the sajda is valid.
D) He must perform additional prostations of forgetfulness.

Key Takeaway
In voluntary prayer, building another pair after sajda sahw invalidates the original sajda, so it must be repeated; an exception exists for a traveler who intends to settle.

Following an Imam with Sajda Sahw Pending: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on following a forgetful imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad/Zufar regarding the validity of following an imam who has salam but has not performed sajda sahw, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah) regarding loud laughter.

Core Idea
Salam after forgetfulness is conditional: it does not fully exit until sajda sahw is performed, affecting the validity of following.

This passage delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the status of the salam when a person has committed forgetfulness (sahw) and has not yet performed the sajda sahw. The key question is whether such a person is still considered in prayer after salam, and therefore whether someone can start following him. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold a conditional view, while Muhammad and Zufar maintain that the salam does not exit at all until sajda sahw. The practical ramifications extend beyond following to the invalidation of wudu by loud laughter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the specific scenario and the point of disagreement? The scenario is a person who has forgetfulness (sahw) gives salam but has not yet performed sajda sahw. The dispute is whether his prayer has ended, and thus whether another person can follow him (in prayer) after his salam.
The term 'following' here refers to a latecomer joining the imam's prayer after the imam has given salam but before sajda sahw.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They hold that following is valid only if the forgetful imam performs sajda sahw. Their reasoning: the salam conditionally exits the prayer, but the need for sajda suspends full exit. If he prostrates, it becomes clear he never exited, so following was valid. If he does not prostrate, it becomes clear he exited at the salam, so following is invalid.
The key term here is 'mawquf' (conditional/suspended).
3
State the position of Muhammad and Zufar
They hold that following is valid even if the imam does not perform sajda sahw. Their reasoning: the salam does not exit the prayer at all until sajda sahw is performed. The imam remains in prayer, so following is valid regardless.
They aim to 'achieve compensation by prostration within the state of prayer' – meaning the sajda must be done while still in prayer.
4
Identify the practical consequences (thamarah)
The difference manifests in two ways: (1) In following: as explained above. (2) In loud laughter (قهقهة) after salam but before sajda sahw. According to Muhammad and Zufar, since the person is still in prayer, loud laughter invalidates wudu and the prayer. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, loud laughter does not invalidate wudu because the prayer has effectively ended.
The text explicitly mentions this second consequence.
5
Note the absence of explicit tarjih
The passage presents both views without declaring one as the mufta bihi. Both are transmitted in the school.
Later Hanafi works may prefer one view; this text simply records the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سلم من عليه سهم فاقتدى به غيره صح إن سجد للسهو عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف؛ لأن سلام من عليه السهو يخرجه عن الصلاة موقوفاً؛ لأن السلام محلل في نفسه، وإنما لا يحلل هنا للحاجة إلى أداء السجود، فإذا سجد تبين أنه لم يخرج فصح الاقتداء به، وإذا تابعه المأموم فيه لم يسجد ثانياً في آخر صلاته، وإن كان ذلك السجود في وسط صلاته، لأنه آخر صلاته حكماً وصلاة الإمام حقيقة، تحقيقاً للمتابعة، فإن سها فيما يقضيه يسجد له أيضاً، ولا يجزئه عند سجوده مع الإمام، كما في (الدراية). (وإلا) أي: وإن لم يسجد الساهي (فلا يصح الاقتداء به؛ لأنه تبين أنه خرج من الصلاة من حين سلم. وقال محمد وزفر: الاقتداء به وإن لم يسجد؛ لأن سلام من عليه السهو لا يخرجه عن الصلاة أصلاً عندهما، ليتحقق الجبر بالسجود في إحرام الصلاة، وثمرة الخلاف ظهرت في الاقتداء وعلمته، وتظهر في انتقاض الطهارة بالقهقهة، فعند محمد وزفر ينتقض لا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف.
And if the one upon whom there is (forgetfulness) gives salam, and someone else follows him in prayer, it is valid if he (the forgetful one) performs prostration for forgetfulness according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; because the salam of one who has forgetfulness upon him takes him out of prayer conditionally; because salam is analytically permissive, but it does not permit here due to the need to perform the prostration. So if he prostrates, it becomes clear that he did not exit, so following him is valid. And if the follower follows him in that prostration, he does not prostrate a second time at the end of his prayer, even though that prostration was in the middle of his prayer, because it is the end of his prayer in legal ruling and the imam's prayer in reality, to achieve following. If he (the follower) forgets in his subsequent prayer, he performs prostration for it also, and it does not suffice him when he prostrates with the imam, as in (al-Diraya). (Otherwise) i.e., if the forgetful one does not prostrate, (the following is not valid); because it is clear that he exited the prayer from the time he gave salam. And Muhammad and Zufar said: following him is valid even if he does not prostrate; because the salam of one with forgetfulness does not take him out of prayer at all according to them, in order to achieve compensation by prostration within the state of prayer. And the fruit of the difference appears in following as you know, and it appears in the invalidation of purification by loud laughter: according to Muhammad and Zufar, it invalidates, not according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (اﻵخر) regarding whether it is valid to follow an imam who has committed forgetfulness (sahw) and has not yet performed sajda sahw. The core issue is whether the salam given by such a person completely exits him from prayer or not. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the salam is conditional: it does not fully exit the prayer until the sajda sahw is performed. Therefore, if the imam performs sajda sahw after salam, it is valid for someone to start following him (as a latecomer in a sense) because the imam is still effectively in prayer. If the imam does not perform sajda sahw, it becomes clear that he had exited at the salam, so following is invalid. Imam Muhammad and Zufar hold that the salam does not exit the prayer at all until sajda sahw is done, so even if the imam does not prostrate immediately, following is still valid because the imam remains in prayer. The practical consequence (ثمرة الخلاف) also appears in whether loud laughter (قهقهة) invalidates wudu and prayer: according to Muhammad and Zufar, it does invalidate because the person is still considered in prayer; according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, laughter after salam but before sajda sahw does not invalidate wudu because the prayer has effectively ended, though sajda sahw is still required.

Key Terms
السلام (al-salām): The concluding salam of the prayer; here it is given by someone who has forgetfulness (sahw) upon him.
موقوف (mawqūf): Conditional or suspended; the exit from prayer is suspended pending the performance of sajda sahw.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarat al-khilāf): The practical consequence or fruit of the disagreement among scholars, i.e., how the difference affects actual rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad and Zufar, what is the ruling if someone follows an imam who has given salam but has not yet performed sajda sahw?
A) Invalid because the imam has exited prayer
B) Valid because the imam is still in prayer
C) Invalid because sajda sahw must be done before salam
D) Valid only if the follower also has sajda sahw

Key Takeaway
The validity of following an imam with sajda sahw pending hinges on whether his salam fully exits him from prayer; Abu Hanifa says conditional exit, Muhammad says no exit.

Building an Additional Shaf' After Sajdah al-Sahw in Nafl
Intra-Hanafi dispute on building after sajdah al-sahw in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on building an additional shaf' after sajdah al-sahw in nafl prayer and distinguish it from the minority intra-Hanafi view.

Core Idea
Building a shaf' after sajdah al-sahw in nafl nullifies the sajdah, requiring repetition.

In supererogatory (nafl) prayers, the Hanafi school has specific rules about building additional units after performing sajdah al-sahw. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether such building invalidates the sajdah, with the later relied-upon view requiring repetition. Understanding this ruling helps avoid common errors in nafl prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that building an additional shaf' (even-numbered unit) after sajdah al-sahw in nafl is makruh tanzih (disliked) based on the majority Hanafi view.
The source states 'لم يَبْنِ... استحباباً' meaning it is prohibited as a recommendation.
2
Trace the majority (mufta bihi) view
If building occurs despite the prohibition, the sajdah al-sahw is nullified and must be repeated. This is the chosen view (al-mukhtar) supported by al-Fath and others.
The reasoning is that building places the sajdah in the middle of prayer, undermining its compensatory japr purpose.
3
Analyze the minority view
Abu Bakr al-A'mash and Abu Ja'far hold that the sajdah remains valid even after building, because it was performed correctly at its proper time.
This view is recorded in al-Fatawa al-Sughra.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The author declares the majority view as 'al-asahh' (most correct) because the first sajdah is nullified by the subsequent building.
The majority view is relied upon for fatwa (mufta bihi).
5
Note the exception for travelers
If a traveler performs sajdah al-sahw and then intends residency, building is allowed because not building would invalidate the entire prayer. This exception highlights that the prohibition on building is specific to nafl where no such necessity exists.
Source: al-Hidayah; the exception does not apply to ordinary nafl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسجد للسهو. ولو سجد للسِّهْوِ في شَفْعِ التَّطوع لم يَيْنِ شَفْعاً آخر عليه، استحباباً، فإن بني أعاد سجود السهو، في المختار. (وسجد للسهو) لتأخير السلام، وتمكن النقصان في الفرض بالخروج لا على الوجه الواجب. (ولو سجد للسهو فِي شَفْعِ التَّطوع لم يَبْنِ شَفْعاً آخرَ عليه) أي: ليس له أن يبني [متمماً آخر عليه ] لأن البناء يبطل السجود بلا ضرورة لوقوعه في وسط الصلاة، وما أداه صحيح بدون البناء، فلا يبني ( استحباباً) لأن الاحتراز عن نقض الواجب أولى كما في البرهان، فإن بني صح لبقاء التحريمة و (أعاد سجود السهو، في المختار ) وقيل : لا يعيده لأنه وقع جابراً حين وقع فيعتد به عند أبي بكر الأعمش، وبه أخذ الفقيه أبو جعفر، كذا في الفتاوى الصغرى، فالأصح أن يعيده لبطلان الأول بما طرأ من البناء، كما في الفتح، وقيدنا بالنفل؛ لأن المسافر إذا سجد للسهو ثم نوى الإقامة فإنه يبني؛ لأنه لو لم يبن يبطل جميع صلاته، كذا في الهداية، ويعيد سجود السهو لبطلان الأول بالبناء، كما في شرح المقدسي.
And he performs sajdah for forgetfulness. If he performed sajdah for forgetfulness in an even-numbered unit (shaf') of supererogatory prayer, he may not build another shaf' upon it, as a recommendation. If he does build, he repeats the sajdah of forgetfulness, according to the chosen (al-mukhtar). (He performs sajdah for forgetfulness) because of delaying the salam, and the deficiency in the obligatory prayer through exiting not in the required manner. (If he performed sajdah for forgetfulness in the shaf' of supererogatory prayer, he does not build another shaf' upon it) meaning: he may not build an additional completion upon it because building invalidates the sajdah without necessity due to its occurrence in the middle of the prayer, and what he performed is valid without building, so he does not build (as a recommendation) because avoiding violation of the obligatory is better, as in al-Burhan. If he builds, it is valid due to the continuing state of consecration (tahrimah), and he repeats the sajdah of forgetfulness according to the chosen. And it is said: he does not repeat it because it occurred as a compensatory act when it occurred, so it is considered valid according to Abu Bakr al-A'mash, and the jurist Abu Ja'far adopted this, as in al-Fatawa al-Sughra. So the most correct is to repeat it because the first is nullified by the building that occurred, as in al-Fath. We restricted it to supererogatory prayer because if a traveler performed sajdah for forgetfulness then intended residency, he builds because if he does not build, all his prayer becomes invalid, as in al-Hidayah. And he repeats the sajdah of forgetfulness because the first is nullified by building, as in Sharh al-Maqdisi.
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a person praying nafl can build an additional shaf' (even-numbered pair) after performing sajdah al-sahw. The author explains that the relied-upon position (al-mukhtar) is that one should not build; doing so invalidates the sajdah, requiring its repetition. The reasoning is that building places the sajdah in the middle of the prayer, nullifying its compensatory purpose. However, a minority view (Abu Bakr al-A'mash and Abu Ja'far) holds that the sajdah remains valid even if building occurs, because it was performed correctly at its time. The author sides with the majority, emphasizing that the first sajdah is nullified by the subsequent building. A contrast is made with a traveler who, after sajdah al-sahw, intends to stay (niyyah iqamah): in that case, building is allowed because not building would invalidate the entire prayer. This exception underscores that the prohibition on building is specific to nafl where no such necessity exists.

Key Terms
سجد للسهو (sajada lil-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness performed to compensate for an omission or error in prayer.
شفع (shaf'): An even-numbered unit of prayer, typically a pair of rak'ahs, especially in nafl prayers (e.g., the two rak'ahs before Fajr).
بناء (bina'): Connecting an additional part to a prayer after it has been concluded, effectively extending the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is recommended, and the sajdah is valid.
C) It is makruh tanzih; if done, the sajdah must be repeated.
D) It invalidates the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
Building an additional shaf' after sajdah al-sahw in nafl prayer is makruh tanzih and nullifies the sajdah, which must be repeated; this is the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Following an Imam Who Owes Sajdah al-Sahw: The Salam Mawquf Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional salam and its practical consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad/Zafar on the validity of following an imam who owes sajdah al-sahw, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to the issues of qahqaha and niyyah iqamah.

Core Idea
The salam of one who owes sajdah is mawquf (conditional): it only fully exits if sajdah is not performed.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the status of a person who gives salam while still obligated to perform sajdah al-sahw. The disagreement centers on whether his salam fully exits him from prayer or only conditionally, and it has practical consequences for the validity of following such an imam, the effect of laughter after salam, and the change of intention for a traveler. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how a single usul principle—the nature of the compensator (jabir)—generates multiple furu' rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf)
Identify the view that the salam of one who owes sajdah conditionally exits him. The salam is a dissolving act in itself, but it is suspended because the sajdah is due. If he performs sajdah, it retroactively shows he never exited, making following him valid.
This view relies on the concept of 'salam mawquf' (conditional salam).
2
Identify the opponent (Muhammad & Zafar)
Note that Muhammad and Zafar hold that the salam does not exit at all. They argue that the sajdah must occur within the state of ihram (consecration) to serve as a compensator, so the salam cannot end the prayer.
This view denies the very possibility of a conditional exit.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent's dalil: the compensator (jabr) must be performed within the prayer's sanctity (hurmah) to be effective. If salam exits, the sajdah would be outside prayer and could not compensate.
This is a qiyas-based argument: sajdah al-sahw is like a rukn that must occur within the act.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf respond that the salam is partially effective; it only fully dissolves if no sajdah is performed. The necessity of the sajdah suspends the full effect, allowing the sajdah to occur as if still in prayer.
Key concept: ta'alluq (suspension) and tabayyun (retroactive clarity).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The difference has three practical consequences: (1) validity of following the imam; (2) invalidation of wudu by laughter (qahqaha) after salam but before sajdah; (3) change of a traveler's prayer from qasr to tamam by intention of residency (niyyah iqamah) after salam before sajdah.
The author defends the validity of niyyah iqamah even if made before sajdah, citing al-Hidayah and al-Dirayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سلَّمَ مَنْ عليه سَهو فاقتدى به غيره صح إِنْ سَجَدَ للسهو عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف؛ لأن سلام من عليه السهو يخرجه عن الصلاة موقوفاً؛ لأن السلام محلل في نفسه، وإنما لا يحلل هنا للحاجة إلى أداء السجود، فإذا سجد تبين أنه لم يخرج فصح الاقتداء به، وإذا تابعه المأموم فيه لم يسجد ثانياً في آخر صلاته، لأنه آخر صلاته حكماً وصلاة الإمام حقيقة، تحقيقاً للمتابعة، فإن سها فيما يقضيه يسجد له أيضاً، ولا يجزئه عند سجوده مع الإمام، كما في الدراية. وإلا فلا يصح الاقتداء به؛ لأنه تبين أنه خرج من الصلاة من حين سلم. وقال محمد وزفر: الاقتداء به وإن لم يسجد؛ لأن سلام من عليه السهو لا يخرجه عن الصلاة أصلاً عندهما، ليتحقق الجبر بالسجود في إحرام الصلاة، وثمرة الخلاف ظهرت في الاقتداء وعلمته، وتظهر في انتقاض الطهارة بالقهقهة، فعند محمد وزفر ينتقض لا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، ولا يتصور أن يسجد بعدها لأنه تَبَيَّنَ بالسلام الأول خروجه للقهقهة، وما في بعض الشروح من أنه إن عاد إلى السجود انتقضت ففيه غفلة. انتهى. وفي الهداية: وتظهر في تغير الفرض بنية الإقامة في هذه الحالة أي: بعد السلام قبل السجود للسهو، وقال في الدراية: فعند محمد يتغير فرضه، وعندهما أي: أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، لا يتغير فرضه سواء سجد للسهو أو لا؛ لأنه لو تغير بالسجود لصحت نيته قبل السجود، ولو صحت لوقعت السجدة في وسط الصلاة ولا يعتد بها، فصار كأنه لم يسجد أصلاً، فلو صحت لصحت بلا سجود، ولا وجه له عندهما لأنه يحصل بعد الخروج فلا يتغير فرضه. انتهى. قلت فيه تأمل، لأن محصله أن عدم صحة نيته الإقامة بتقديره لم يسجد أصلاً وقد سجد، وهو إذا لم يسجد أصلاً لا تصح نيته الإقامة، وقد صرح في الدراية: بأنه إذا سجد للسهو وهو مسافر فنوى الإقامة صحت نيته، ويتم أربعاً. انتهى. فيكون الحكم كذلك هنا بجامع وجود السجود في الصورتين، ولا يفترق الحال بتقديم نية الإقامة على سجود السهو للزوم التناقض، وقول الكمال وعندهما، أي أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف: لا يتغير فرضه بنيته الإقامة، لأن النية لم تحصل في حرمة الصلاة. انتهى غير مسلم وقد صرح هو بخلافه في عدة مواضع منها قوله: سلام من عليه السهو لا يخرجه عن حرمة الصلاة، وصرّح به صاحب الهداية، في مسائل البناء في شفع التطوع بعد سجوده للسهو فيه، وصرح بما ذكرناه في غاية البيان. وقول صاحب البحر: أنه، أي: قول غاية البيان) غلط، لأنه لو سجد فقد عاد إلى حرمة الصلاة، فيتغير فرضه أربعاً، فيقع سجوده في خلال الصلاة فلا يعتد به فلا فائدة في الاشتغال به انتهى ليس بذاك بل قول غاية البيان صحيح بواضح البرهان، ويلزم صاحب البحر أن نية الإقامة بعد سجوده للسهو لا تصح، لوقوع السجود في خلال الصلاة، وهم متفقون على صحتها، ومنهم صاحب الهداية صرح قبل هذا بقوله: بخلاف المسافر إذا سجد للسهو ثم نوى الإقامة يبني، لأنه لو لم يبن يبطل جميع الصلاة. انتهى. لأنه كذلك هنا لأن نية الإقامة وإن تقدمت على سجود السهو فهي مصاحبة له، وإلا يلزم تخلف الحكم إذا قارنت نية الإقامة السجود. انتهى. وقد قال الكمال: إن الجابر واقع في حرمة الصلاة اتفاقاً بينهم، وتراخي الحكم وهو التحلل عن العلة وهي السلام عند محمد وزفر لضرورة الجابر وهو سجود السهو. انتهى. فتأمل. ( ويسجد للسهو ) أي: يجب على من سها عن واجب أن يسجد للسهو (وإن سلم عامداً)؛ مريــداً كون سلامه (للقطعِ) والخروج عن حرمة الصلاة؛ لأن نيته تغيير المشروع وهو القطع، ليترتب عليه ترك السجود، والنية المجردة عن عمل غير مستحق عليه، لا تؤثر في إبطال ما ركنه إعمال الجوارح.
If one who owes a sajdah for forgetfulness gives the salam, and another person follows him (as a muqtadi), it is valid if he (the forgetful one) performs the sajdah for forgetfulness, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because the salam of one who owes sajdah takes him out of the prayer conditionally; for the salam is a dissolving element in itself, but it does not dissolve here due to the need to perform the sajdah. So if he performs sajdah, it becomes clear that he did not exit, so following him is valid. And if the follower joins him in that sajdah, he does not perform a second sajdah at the end of his prayer, because it is his prayer's end in ruling, and the imam's prayer is actual, in realization of followership. If the follower errs in what he is completing, he also prostrates for it, but it does not suffice him when he prostrates with the imam, as in al-Dirayah. Otherwise (if he does not perform sajdah), following him is not valid, because it becomes clear that he exited from prayer from the time he gave salam. Muhammad and Zafar said: following him is valid even if he does not perform sajdah, because in their view the salam of one who owes sajdah does not remove him from the prayer at all, so that the compensation (jabr) is achieved by the sajdah within the prayer's consecration. The fruit of the difference appears in following, as you know, and appears in the invalidation of purification (taharah) by laughter (qahqaha): according to Muhammad and Zafar, it is invalidated; according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it is not. And it is inconceivable that he prostrates after it because it became clear by the first salam that he exited due to laughter. What is in some commentaries that if he returns to prostration it is invalidated is a heedlessness. End. In al-Hidayah: It appears in the change of the obligatory prayer by the intention of residency (niyyah iqamah) in this case, i.e., after salam before sajdah for forgetfulness. In al-Dirayah: According to Muhammad, his obligatory prayer changes; according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), his obligatory prayer does not change, whether he performs sajdah for forgetfulness or not. Because if it changed by sajdah, his intention would be valid before sajdah, and if valid, the sajdah would occur in the middle of prayer and would not be considered valid, so it would be as if he did not perform sajdah at all. So if it were valid, it would be valid without sajdah, and there is no justification for it in their view because it occurs after exiting, so his obligatory prayer does not change. End. I say: There is reflection in this, because its gist is that his intention of residency is not valid, presuming he had not performed sajdah at all, while he did perform sajdah. And if he had not performed sajdah at all, his intention of residency would not be valid. And it is explicitly stated in al-Dirayah that if he performs sajdah for forgetfulness while a traveler and then intends residency, his intention is valid and he completes four rak'ahs. End. So the ruling is the same here due to the common factor of the existence of sajdah in both cases, and the situation does not differ by bringing the intention of residency forward before sajdah for forgetfulness, due to the inevitability of contradiction. The statement of al-Kamal: 'In their view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), his obligatory prayer does not change by his intention of residency because the intention did not occur within the sanctity of prayer' is not accepted, and he (al-Kamal) himself stated the contrary in several places, including his saying: 'The salam of one who owes sajdah does not remove him from the sanctity of prayer.' This is explicitly stated by the author of al-Hidayah, in the issues of building in the shaf' of supererogatory prayer after his sajdah for forgetfulness therein, and he explicitly stated what we mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan. The statement of the author of al-Bahr: 'That (the statement of Ghayat al-Bayan) is an error, because if he performed sajdah, he has returned to the sanctity of prayer, so his obligatory prayer changes to four, so his sajdah occurs in the midst of prayer and is not considered valid, so there is no benefit in engaging in it' is not correct. Rather, the statement of Ghayat al-Bayan is correct with clear proof. It follows from the statement of the author of al-Bahr that the intention of residency after his sajdah for forgetfulness is not valid, due to the occurrence of sajdah in the midst of prayer, while they agree on its validity. Among them, the author of al-Hidayah explicitly stated before this: 'Contrary to the traveler who performs sajdah for forgetfulness and then intends residency: he builds, because if he does not build, all his prayer becomes invalid.' End. Because it is so here, for the intention of residency, even if it precedes the sajdah for forgetfulness, is concomitant with it, otherwise the ruling would be delayed when the intention of residency coincides with the sajdah. End. And al-Kamal said: The compensator (jabir) occurs within the sanctity of prayer by agreement among them, and the delay of the ruling (the dissolution) from the cause (the salam) is due to the necessity of the compensator (sajdah al-sahw) according to Muhammad and Zafar. End. Reflect. (And he performs sajdah for forgetfulness) meaning: it is obligatory on one who forgets an obligatory element to perform sajdah for forgetfulness, (even if he gave salam intentionally) intending his salam for termination and exit from the sanctity of prayer, because his intention changes the prescribed act (finishing the prayer) to termination, so that his omission of sajdah follows from it. A mere intention without action that he is not required to perform does not affect the invalidation of a act whose pillar is the use of limbs.
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the status of a person who owes sajdah al-sahw and gives salam. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the salam conditionally exits the person from prayer; it only becomes a full exit if he does not perform the sajdah. Therefore, if he does perform sajdah, it retroactively shows he never left, making it valid for someone to follow him (as muqtadi) after his salam. If he skips sajdah, the follower's prayer is invalid. Muhammad and Zafar hold that the salam does not exit him at all, so following is valid even without sajdah. The practical implications (thamarah al-khilaf) extend to several areas: (1) Laughter (qahqaha) during prayer: if the imam laughs after salam but before sajdah, according to Muhammad and Zafar his wudu is invalidated (since he is still in prayer), but according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf his wudu remains intact because he already exited. (2) Change of intention (niyyah iqamah) for a traveler: if a traveler gives salam before performing sajdah al-sahw and then intends to stay, Muhammad holds that his prayer becomes full (four rak'ahs), while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it remains two rak'ahs. The author then engages in a lengthy critique of positions from al-Dirayah, al-Hidayah, and Ghayat al-Bayan, defending the view that the intention of residency is valid even if made before the sajdah, as long as sajdah follows. Finally, the passage affirms the general obligation of sajdah al-sahw for any omission of a wajib, even if one intentionally gave salam to exit, because intention alone cannot override the actual obligation.

Key Terms
سلام موقوف (salam mawquf): A conditional salam that neither fully exits nor retains one in prayer; its effect is suspended pending the performance of sajdah al-sahw.
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud, audible laughter that invalidates wudu and prayer according to Hanafis.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarah al-khilaf): The practical consequences resulting from a legal disagreement between scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what is the status of a person who gives salam while owing sajdah al-sahw, and what happens if he performs the sajdah?
A) He fully exits the prayer; performing sajdah later does not change anything.
B) He conditionally exits; performing sajdah retroactively shows he never exited, making following him valid.
C) He does not exit at all; his prayer continues until sajdah is performed.
D) He exits the prayer but must still perform sajdah outside of prayer.

Key Takeaway
The salam of one who owes sajdah al-sahw is conditional (mawquf); this generates multiple practical differences between the views of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad/Zafar, including the validity of following the imam, the effect of laughter, and the change of a traveler's prayer by intention of residency.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Traveler's Intention After Salam Before Sajdah al-Sahw
Dispute on whether intending residence changes prayer obligation after salam before sajdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) on whether a traveler's intention of residence after salam but before sajdah al-sahw changes the fard, and evaluate the tarjih based on the commentary.

Core Idea
Salam by a forgetful person does not exit the prayer's inviolability until sajdah al-sahw is performed, allowing intention of residence to change the fard.

This passage presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute about a traveler who, after concluding his prayer with salam, intends to establish residence before performing the necessary sajdah al-sahw. The central question is whether this intention changes the obligatory prayer from two rak'ahs (qasr) to four (full prayer). By studying this debate, you will understand how the Hanafi school reasons about the inviolability of prayer (hurmah al-salah) and the role of sajdah al-sahw in maintaining it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
A traveler performs a 2-rak'ah prayer, then gives salam (forgetfully), and before performing sajdah al-sahw, he intends to establish residence. Does his fard change to 4 rak'ahs?
The salam is due to forgetfulness (sahw), not intentional cutting.
2
State the position of Muhammad al-Shaybani
According to Muhammad, the fard does change: the traveler must now pray 4 rak'ahs total. The sajdah al-sahw remains valid and is performed after completing the additional rak'ahs.
Muhammad's view is supported by the text from al-Dirayah.
3
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Sahibayn)
According to the Sahibayn, the fard does not change; the intention of residence is ineffective because it occurs after the salam, which they consider to exit the prayer's inviolability. The sajdah al-sahw, if performed, would be invalid.
Their reasoning: if the fard changed, the intention would be valid before sajdah, causing sajdah mid-prayer, which is invalid.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn
The author argues that the Sahibayn's premise is flawed: the salam of a forgetful person does not exit the prayer's inviolability. Citing al-Dirayah, if a traveler performs sajdah first and then intends residence, the intention is valid. The same logic applies when intention precedes sajdah, as the intention 'accompanies' the sajdah.
Key evidence: al-Hidayah states that salam of a forgetful person does not remove him from the prayer's sanctity.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentary favors Muhammad's view. The relied-upon position is that the intention of residence changes the fard, and the sajdah remains valid.
The author refutes objections from al-Bahr and others, asserting the correctness of Muhammad's position with 'clear proof'.

الفرض بنية الإقامة في هـ الحالة أي: بعد السلام قبل السجود للسهو، وقال في ( الدراية » : فعند محمد يتغير فرضه، وعندهما أي: أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، لا يتغير فرضه سواء سجد للسهو أو لا؛ لأنه لو تغير بالسجود لصحت نيته قبل السجود، ولو صحت لوقعت السجدة في وسط الصلاة ولا يعتد بها، فصار كأنه لم يسجد أصلاً، فلو صحت لصحت بلا سجود، ولا وجه له عندهما لأنه يحصل بعد الخروج فلا يتغير فرضه. انتهى. قلت فيه تأمل، لأن محصله أن عدم صحة نيته الإقامة بتقديره لم يسجد أصلا وقـد سجد، وهو إذا لم يسجد أصلاً لا : تصح نيته الإقامة، وقد صرح في ( الدراية » : بأنه إذا سجد للسهو وهو مسافر فنوى الإقامة صحت نيته، ويتم أربعاً. لأن النية لم تحصل في حرمة الصلاة. انتهى غير مسلم وقد صرح هو بخلافه في عدة مواضع منها قوله: ســلام مـن عـلـيـه السهو لا يخرجه عن حرمة الصلاة، وصرّح به صاحب ( الهداية » ، في مسائل البناء في شـفـع التطوع بعد سجوده للسهو فيه، وصرح بما ذكرناه في غاية البيان » . وقول صاحب « البحر » : أنه، أي: قـول غاية البيان) غلط، لأنه لو سجد فقد عاد إلى حرمة الصلاة، فيتغير فرضه أربعاً، فيقع سجوده في خلال الصلاة فلا And he performs sajdah al-sahw, even if he intended to terminate the prayer by giving salam. He performs it after because it became clear through the first salam that he intended laughing. And what is in some commentaries that if he returns to this sajdah it is invalid is careless. End. In al-Hidayah: It appears in changing the fard by intention of residence in this situation, i.e., after salam before sajdah al-sahw. And in al-Dirayah: According to Muhammad his fard changes; according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) his fard does not change whether he performs sajdah al-sahw or not; because if it changed by sajdah, his intention would be valid before sajdah, and if valid the sajdah would occur in the middle of the prayer and would not count, so it would be as if he had not performed sajdah at all. Thus if it were valid it would be valid without sajdah, and there is no basis for that according to them because it occurs after exiting, so his fard does not change. End. I say there is reflection, because its gist is that the invalidity of his intention of residence, if he had not performed sajdah at all, and he did perform sajdah; and if he had not performed sajdah at all, his intention of residence is not valid. And it is stated explicitly in al-Dirayah: If he performs sajdah al-sahw while traveling and then intends residence, his intention is valid and he completes four. End. So the ruling applies here due to the commonality of the existence of sajdah in both cases, and the case does not differ by advancing the intention of residence before sajdah al-sahw due to necessity of contradiction. And the statement of al-Kamal: According to them, i.e., Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, his fard does not change by his intention of residence because the intention was not made within the inviolability of the prayer. End, but it is not accepted. And he himself stated the contrary in several places, including his statement: The salam of one who is forgetful does not remove him from the inviolability of the prayer. And the author of al-Hidayah stated it in the issues of building upon the supererogatory pair after his sajdah al-sahw therein, and the author of Ghayat al-Bayan stated what we mentioned. And the statement of the author of al-Bahr: That is, the statement of Ghayat al-Bayan is a mistake, because if he performed sajdah, he returns to the inviolability of the prayer, so his fard changes to four, so his sajdah occurs during the prayer and is not counted, so there is no benefit in occupying oneself with it – end. This is not correct; rather the statement of Ghayat al-Bayan is correct with clear proof. And it would follow for the author of al-Bahr that the intention of residence after his sajdah al-sahw is not valid, because the sajdah occurs during the prayer, and they agree on its validity, including the author of al-Hidayah who stated before this: Contrary to a traveler who performs sajdah al-sahw then intends residence – he builds, because if he does not build the entire prayer becomes invalid. End. It is likewise here because the intention of residence, even if advanced before sajdah al-sahw, accompanies it; otherwise it would necessitate that the ruling lags when the intention of residence coincides with the sajdah. End. And al-Kamal said: The compensatory [prostration] occurs within the inviolability of the prayer by agreement among them, and the delay of the ruling – i.e., the dissolution from the cause, which is salam according to Muhammad and Zufar – is due to the necessity of the compensatory [prostration], i.e., sajdah al-sahw. End. So reflect.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a traveler who, after concluding his prayer with salam (intentionally or due to forgetfulness), intends to establish residence before performing the necessary sajdah al-sahw. The issue is whether this intention changes the obligatory form of the prayer from two rak'ahs (traveler's qasr) to four (full prayer). The author first cites al-Hidayah, which notes that the change of fard becomes apparent in such a case. Then from al-Dirayah, three positions are reported: Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the fard changes; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it does not change, regardless of whether sajdah is performed. Their reasoning is that if the sajdah were to change the fard, the intention of residence would be valid before the sajdah; but then the sajdah would occur within the prayer (since the intention would keep the prayer's inviolability), rendering the sajdah invalid, as compensation cannot be performed mid-prayer. Thus the sajdah would be as if not done, and the intention would be valid without it – an impossibility. The author then critiques the Sahibayn's view, arguing from al-Dirayah itself: if a traveler performs sajdah al-sahw and then intends residence, his intention is valid and he completes four rak'ahs. This shows that sajdah after salam does not negate the prayer's inviolability, contrary to the Sahibayn's assumption. The author supports his position with statements from al-Kamal and al-Hidayah, emphasizing that the salam of a forgetful person does not exit one from the prayer's sanctity. He refutes the objection from al-Bahr that sajdah after salam would re-enter the prayer and invalidate the sajdah, arguing that the intention of residence can coexist with the sajdah. The passage concludes with al-Kamal's explanation that the compensatory prostration occurs within the prayer's inviolability by consensus, and the delay of dissolution (tahallul) from the cause (salam) is due to the necessity of the sajdah. The mufta bihi position seems to be that the intention of residence after salam but before sajdah changes the fard, as supported by the author's critique.

Key Terms
نية الإقامة (niyyah al-iqāmah): The intention of a traveler to establish residence in a place, which changes the ruling of qasr (shortening) to full prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The prayer is nullified and must be repeated.
D) The traveler must repeat both the sajdah and the prayer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the salam of a forgetful person does not exit the prayer's inviolability, so an intention of residence made before sajdah al-sahw changes the fard from qasr to full, as upheld by Imam Muhammad.

Sajdah al-Sahw After Intentional Salam: The Remaining Sanctity of Prayer
Explanation of the ruling and conditions for sajdah al-sahw after intentional salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that sajdah al-sahw is wajib even after intentional salam, and identify the two actions that nullify the prayer's sanctity, preventing the prostration.

Core Idea
Intentional salam does not end the prayer's sanctity; sajdah al-sahw remains wajib until you turn away or speak.

You might think that saying 'assalamu alaykum' with the intention to end the prayer immediately cuts off all connection to it. But in the Hanafi school, the prayer's inviolability (ḥurmat al-ṣalāh) lingers — allowing you to perform forgetfulness prostrations even after salam. This lesson unpacks why a mere intention to terminate doesn't override a physical obligation, and what actions truly close the door.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states: 'He performs sajdah al-sahw even if he gave salam intentionally.' Determine the hukm level: fard or wajib?
Hanafis classify sajdah al-sahw as wajib, not fard, because its proof is zannī.
2
Understand the concept of prayer's sanctity (ḥurmah)
The commentator distinguishes between the essence of prayer (ḥaqīqah) and its inviolability (ḥurmah). Intentional salam invalidates the essence, but the sanctity remains for corrective actions.
This distinction is key to the Hanafi position.
3
Identify the nullifiers of sanctity
The text lists two actions that break the ḥurmah: turning away from the qibla and speaking. Until these occur, sajdah al-sahw can still be performed.
Some authorities add leaving the mosque as equivalent to speaking.
4
Contrast with leaving a fard rukn
If someone leaves a fard rukn (like a ṣulbiyyah prostration) and intentionally says salam while remembering it, the prayer is invalid because the rukn belongs to the essence, which is already nullified.
This contrast proves that sajdah al-sahw belongs to the sanctity, not the essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( ويسجد للسهو) أي: يجب على من سها عن واجب أن يسجد للسهو (وإن سلم عامداً)؛ مريــداً كون سلامه (للقطعِ) والخروج عن حرمة الصلاة؛ لأن نيته تغيير المشروع وهو القطع، ليترتب عـلـيـه ترك السجود، والنية المجردة عن عمل غير مستحق عليه، لا يؤثر في إبطال ما ركنه إعمال الجوارح، وهو سجود السهو فلغت نيته وقيدنا العمل بكونه غير مستحق عليه، ليندفع ما يقال: هذه مقرونة بالعمل، وهو التسليم فيسجد للسهو ( ما لم يتحوّل عن القبلة، أو يتكلّم) فإنهما يبطلان التحريمة، وقيل: لا يقطـع بالتحول ما لم يتكلم، أو يخرج من المسجد كما في « الدرر » ، عن « النهاية » ، بخلاف ما إذا ترك سجدة صلبية، أو فرضاً وسلم متذكراً له حيث تفسد صلاته، لأنه يؤتى به في حقيقة الصلاة، وقد بطلت بالسلام العمد، وأما سجود السهو فيؤتى به في حرمة الصلاة، وهي باقية، ولغت نيه القطع لما ذكرنا.
(And he performs sajdah al-sahw) i.e., he obligated upon one who omits a wajib to perform sajdah al-sahw (even if he gave salam intentionally); intending his salam to be for termination and exit from the inviolability of the prayer; because his intention is to change the prescribed action, which is termination, so that leaving the sajdah is arranged accordingly. And a mere intention without an action that is not owed upon him does not affect the invalidation of that whose pillar is the action of the limbs, which is sajdah al-sahw. So his intention becomes void. And we qualified the action as not owed upon him to repel what is said: This intention is coupled with the action, which is the salam, so he performs sajdah al-sahw (as long as he has not turned away from the qibla, or spoken) for these two invalidate the tahrimah. And it is said: Turning away does not terminate unless he speaks or leaves the mosque, as in al-Durar from al-Nihayah. Contrary to the case where he leaves a fard rukn (salbiyyah) or a fard and gives salam while being mindful of it, where his prayer is invalidated; because that rukn is performed within the essence of the prayer, and the prayer has already been nullified by intentional salam. As for sajdah al-sahw, it is performed within the inviolability of the prayer, which still remains, and his intention of termination becomes void for what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn ruling that sajdah al-sahw must be performed even if one intentionally says salam to terminate the prayer. The commentator explains that the intention to terminate does not invalidate the need for sajdah because sajdah al-sahw is a pillar that involves physical action, and a mere intention cannot undo an obligation that requires physical performance. The key condition is that the person has not turned away from the qibla or spoken after the salam; if he does either, the tahrimah (initial sanctity of prayer) is broken and the prayer is truly ended, making sajdah al-sahw impossible. The passage also distinguishes between leaving a fard rukn (like a prostration from the prayer itself) and leaving sajdah al-sahw. If one leaves a fard rukn and intentionally says salam while mindful of it, the prayer is invalid because that rukn is part of the prayer's essence, which was already nullified by the intentional salam. However, sajdah al-sahw is performed within the remaining inviolability of the prayer, which persists until the person actually exits by turning away or speaking. The commentator cites a variant view from al-Durar that turning away alone does not terminate unless accompanied by speech or leaving the mosque. The proof is analogical: just as a fard rukn cannot be performed after intentional salam because the prayer is already invalid, sajdah al-sahw is different because it belongs to the prayer's inviolability, which remains. The effective cause (illa) is that the prayer's sanctity (hurmah) persists after salam for the purposes of compensation.

Key Terms
حرمة الصلاة (ḥurmat al-ṣalāh): The inviolability or sanctity of the prayer that persists even after salam until the person exits by turning away or speaking.
سجدة صلبية (sajdah ṣulbiyyah): A prostration that is an integral part of the prayer (rukn), not a compensatory prostration.
تحريمة (taḥrīmah): The initial prohibition (sanctification) that enters the worshipper into the state of prayer; used here to refer to the prayer's inviolability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What action nullifies the prayer's sanctity after intentional salam, making sajdah al-sahw impossible?
A) Intending to terminate the prayer.
B) Turning away from the qibla or speaking.
C) Performing sajdah al-sahw.
D) Remaining silent and still.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, intentional salam preserves the prayer's sanctity for compensatory sajdah al-sahw, which is only impossible if the worshipper turns away or speaks.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Multiple Sajdahs After Salam: Order and the Effect of Mindfulness
Rulings on multiple sajdahs after salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the order of performing missed sajdahs (tilawah, sahw, salbiyyah) after salam and state whether the prayer is valid based on the person's state of mindfulness.

Core Idea
Mindfulness at salam determines whether missed obligations can be made up; order matters.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rulings when a person has multiple outstanding sajdahs after giving salam. The key distinction is whether the person was mindful (dhakir) of those obligations at the time of salam. If not mindful, the salam is not terminating and the prayer's sanctity remains, allowing the missed acts to be performed in a specific order. If mindful, the salam terminates and the prayer ends, causing the obligations to drop (except when a fard rukn like a missed sajdah is involved, which may invalidate the prayer). We will work through the cases step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of outstanding sajdahs
Determine whether the obligations are tilawah (recitation prostration), sahw (forgetful prostration), or salbiyyah (missed fard sajdah). Each has different legal weight.
2
Assess mindfulness at the time of salam
Ask: Was the person mindful (dhakir) of all, some, or none of the obligations? This determines if the salam is terminating.
If mindful of all, salam is terminating and obligations drop. If not mindful of at least one, salam is not terminating.
3
Apply the order for making up obligations
For non-terminating salam, perform in order: first salbiyyah (if any), then tilawah (if any), then tashahhud and salam, then sajdah sahw, then tashahhud and salam.
Intention (niyyah) is required for each missed sajdah.
4
Handle the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
According to a narration from Abu Yusuf, if the missed fard sajdah is from the second rak'ah, sajdah sahw may suffice. The majority view requires specific make-up.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: لو سلم وعليه تلاوية وسهوية وهو غير ذاكر لهما، أو ذاكر للسهو فقط، لا بـ يعد سلامه قاطعاً، فيسجد للتلاوة، ثم يتشهد لرفعها القعود ويسلم، ثم يسجد للسهو ويتشهد لرفعها التشهد ويسلم، وإن سلم وكان ذاكراً لهما أو للتلاوية فقط كان قاطعاً، وسقطت عنه التلاوية والسهو، لامتناع البناء بسبب القطع، إلا إذا تذكر أنه لم يتشهد، ويسجد للتلاوة وصلاته تامة، وإن سلم وعليه صلبية وسهوية غير ذاكر لهما، أو ذاكراً للسهوية فقط، لم يكن سلامه قاطعاً، ويفعل كالأول، وإن كان ذاكراً لهما وللصلبية خاصة فهو قاطع، فتفسد صلاته، ولو سلم وعليه صلبية وتلاوية وسهوية غير ذاكــر لهنَّ، أو ذاكراً للسهوية لم يقطع ويقضي الأولين مرتباً الأول فالأول، وهـو يـفـيـد وجـوب النيـة في المقضى من السجدات، ثم يتشهد ويسلّم ثم يسجد للسهو. انتهى. قلت: نـص عـلـى لــزوم النيـة في المقضى من السجدات، في ( التجنيس قال : لو سلم في الفجر وعليه سهو فسجد له، ثم تكلم فتذكر أنه ترك صلبية من الركعة الأولى فسدت صلاته، لأنها صارت ديناً في ذمتـه وانـعـدمـت نـيـة القضـاء، وإن كانت من الركعة الثانية لا تفسد إلا في رواية عن أبي يوسف؛ لأنها لم تصـر ديناً في ذمته، فنابت سجدة السهو عن الصلبية، ولو كانت المسألة بحالها، إلا أنه لما سلم للفجر تذكر أن عليـه سجدة تلاوة فسجد لها، ثم تكلم، ثم تذكر أن عليه صلبية فصلاته فاسدة في الوجهين؛ لأن سجدة التلاوة دين عليه فانصرفت نيته إلى قضاء الدين فلا تنصرف السجدة إلى غير القضاء. انتهى. ثم قال الكمال: وإن كان ذاكراً للصلبية أو التلاوية فسدت، وكان سلامه قاطعاً، وإذا سلم وعليه السهو وتكبير التشريق والتلبية لا يسقط عنه ذلك كله، سواء كان ذاكراً للكل، أو ساهياً عن الكل، فيقدم السهو، ثم تكبير التشريق، ثم التلبية، ولو قدم التلبية قبل السهو [ سقطت ] سجدتا السهو والتكبير، ولو لبى قبل التكبير يسقط التكبير، ولو سلم وعليه صلبية وتلاوية وسهو وتكبير التشريق والتلبية، غير ذاكر لها، فعل ذلك على هذا الترتيب، ولو بدأ بالتلبية فسدت، ولو بالتكبير لا تفسد.
Warning: If he gives salam and has upon him [obligations of] tilawah and sahw, and he is not mindful of both, or he is mindful only of sahw, his salam is not considered terminating. So he performs sajdah for tilawah, then performs tashahhud for its sitting and gives salam, then performs sajdah for sahw and performs tashahhud for its tashahhud and gives salam. If he gives salam and is mindful of both or of tilawah only, his salam is terminating, and the tilawah and sahw drop from him, due to the impossibility of building because of the termination, except if he remembers that he did not perform tashahhud, and he performs sajdah for tilawah and his prayer is complete. If he gives salam and has upon him [obligations of] salbiyyah and sahw, not mindful of both, or mindful only of sahw, his salam is not terminating, and he does as the first. If he is mindful of both and especially salbiyyah, it is terminating and his prayer is invalid. If he gives salam and has upon him salbiyyah, tilawah, and sahw, not mindful of them, or mindful of sahw, he does not terminate and he makes up the first two in order, the first before the second. This indicates the obligation of intention in the made-up sajdahs. Then he performs tashahhud and gives salam, then performs sajdah for sahw. End. I say: He textually stated the necessity of intention in the made-up sajdahs in al-Tajnis. He said: If he gives salam in Fajr and has upon him sahw, and he performs sajdah for it, then speaks, then remembers that he left a salbiyyah from the first rak'ah, his prayer is invalid because it becomes a debt upon him and the intention of making up was absent. If it was from the second rak'ah, it is not invalid except in a narration from Abu Yusuf; because it did not become a debt upon him, so the sajdah al-sahw suffices for the salbiyyah. If the case is the same, but when he gave salam for Fajr he remembered that he had a tilawah sajdah, so he performed it, then spoke, then remembered that he had a salbiyyah, his prayer is invalid in both cases; because the tilawah sajdah is a debt upon him, so his intention turned to paying the debt, and the sajdah does not turn to other than the debt. End. Then al-Kamal said: If he is mindful of the salbiyyah or tilawah, it is invalid and his salam is terminating. If he gives salam and has upon him sahw and takbir al-tashriq and talbiyah, none of that drops from him, whether he is mindful of all or forgetful of all. He gives precedence to sahw, then takbir al-tashriq, then talbiyah. If he gives talbiyah before sahw, the two sajdahs of sahw and the takbir drop. If he performs talbiyah before takbir, the takbir drops. If he gives salam and has upon him salbiyyah, tilawah, sahw, takbir al-tashriq, and talbiyah, not mindful of them, he does that in this order. If he begins with talbiyah, it is invalid; if with takbir, it is not invalid.
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage is a detailed set of cases (furu') concerning a person who gives salam while various obligatory actions remain upon him. These include sajdah tilawah (prostration of recitation), sajdah sahw (prostration for forgetfulness), and missed fard prostrations (salbiyyah), as well as takbir al-tashriq and talbiyah. The key factors are whether the person was mindful (dhakir) of these obligations at the time of salam and the order of performance. The passage begins with a warning (tanbih) that if one has both tilawah and sahw and is not mindful of either, or only mindful of sahw, the salam is not terminating, meaning the prayer's sanctity remains. The person then performs the missed actions in a specific order: first sajdah tilawah with its tashahhud and salam, then sajdah sahw with its tashahhud and salam. If he is mindful of both or of tilawah only, the salam becomes terminating, and both sajdahs drop, except if he remembers not having performed tashahhud. If a fard rukn (salbiyyah) is missed along with sahw, similar distinctions apply. The passage then cites al-Tajnis with a specific example: a person who forgets a fard sajdah (salbiyyah) from the first rak'ah after having performed sajdah sahw and then speaking. The sajdah sahw cannot compensate for the fard sajdah because the fard sajdah becomes a debt requiring specific intention. If the missed fard sajdah is from the second rak'ah, according to one narration from Abu Yusuf, sajdah sahw may suffice. But if one has a tilawah sajdah after salam, then speaks, then remembers a salbiyyah, the prayer is invalid because the tilawah sajdah was a debt and the intention for the salbiyyah was not present. Finally, the passage covers cases where multiple obligations include takbir al-tashriq and talbiyah, which have their own order of precedence. The overall principle is that the order must be followed, and memory at the time of salam determines whether compensation is possible.

Key Terms
تلاوية (tilāwiyyah): Sajdah tilawah: the prostration of recitation, wajib when reciting or hearing certain Quranic verses.
سهوية (sahwiyyah): Sajdah sahw: the prostration for forgetfulness, performed to compensate for certain forgetfulness in prayer.
صلبية (ṣulbiyyah): A fard prostration that is an integral part of the prayer (rukn), as opposed to sajdah al-sahw or tilawah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person gives salam and is mindful of having a missed fard sajdah (salbiyyah) but not mindful of sajdah sahw, what is the ruling?
A) The salam is not terminating; he performs sajdah sahw first, then salbiyyah.
B) The salam is terminating; the prayer is invalid because he was mindful of salbiyyah.
C) The salam is not terminating; he performs salbiyyah first, then sajdah sahw.
D) The prayer is valid; both obligations drop.

Key Takeaway
When multiple sajdahs are owed after salam, the order and validity depend on whether the person was mindful at the time of salam.
